Metaphorical Use of 'Khāliq' for Servants
Author explains metaphorical use of 'khāliq' for servants when coupled with God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Qur'anic phrase 'best of creators' does not imply that servants are true creators, and how the term 'khāliq' can be applied metaphorically when paired with God.

Core Idea
Only God is truly Creator; any other use of 'khāliq' is metaphorical when paired with Him.

This passage addresses a potential objection from the Qur'anic phrase 'the best of creators,' which might seem to allow the title 'creator' for others. The author explains that while the servant is a doer (fāʿil), creation belongs exclusively to God. He then provides analogies from Arabic usage to show how a name can be shared in a compound without implying independent possession.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation. Notice the analogies used.
The passage begins with a Qur'anic reference that may be unfamiliar.
2
Identify the main argument
The author argues that the servant is a doer, not a creator, and that 'khāliq' can be applied metaphorically when paired.
3
Examine the analogies
Look at the examples: 'the two Umars' for Abu Bakr and Umar, and 'two moons' for sun and moon. Understand how they illustrate shared naming in a compound.
4
Apply the principle
Consider how this reasoning resolves the apparent contradiction in the Qur'anic phrase 'best of creators'.
This reinforces the doctrine of tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأنت تفري ما خلقت وبعض القوم يخلق ثم لا يفري فكانت الآية محمولة عليه دفعًا للتناقض عن الآيات والدلائل، على أن العبد يكون فاعلاً ولا يكون خالقًا، والله تعالى هو الخالق، ويجوز إطلاق اسم الخالق على العبد وإن لم يكن خالقا إذا ضم إلى الخالق كما يقال: سنة العمرين في أبي بكر رضي الله عنهما – وإن كان أبو بكر لا يسمى عند الانفراد عمر، وكذا يقال للشمس والقمر قمران قال القائل: أخذنا بآفاق السماء عليكم لنا قمراها والنجوم الطوالع وإن كان اسم القمر لا يطلق على الشمس عند الانفراد فكذا هذا
And you cut what you created, and some people create but then do not cut. So the verse is interpreted accordingly to avoid contradiction between verses and proofs, indicating that the servant is a doer (fāʿil) and not a creator (khāliq), and God Most High is the Creator. It is permissible to apply the name 'creator' to the servant even though he is not a creator when coupled with the Creator, just as it is said: 'the way of the two Umars' regarding Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with them both – even though Abu Bakr alone is not called Umar. Similarly, the sun and moon are called 'two moons' (qamarān). The poet said: 'We took to the horizons of the sky against you, for us are its two moons and the rising stars,' even though the name 'moon' is not applied to the sun alone. So this is similar.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage addresses a potential objection from opponents who cite the Qur'anic phrase 'the best of creators' (aḥsan al-khāliqīn), which seems to imply that there are other creators besides God. The author explains that the term 'khāliq' can be applied to servants metaphorically when paired with God, just as 'Umar' is not applied to Abu Bakr alone but 'the two Umars' is used for both, and 'moon' is not applied to the sun alone but 'two moons' is used for both. The key doctrinal point is that the servant is a doer (fāʿil) but not a creator in the true sense; creation (takhlīq) is exclusive to God. The argument follows the author's own order: first stating the problem, then giving the principle that the servant is a doer and not a creator, then providing analogies from common Arabic usage to show that a name can be shared in a compound while being exclusive in isolation.

Key Terms
خالق (khāliq)
فاعل (fāʿil)
العبد (al-ʿabd)
إطلاق (iṭlāq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Qur'anic phrase 'best of creators' implies that humans can be creators alongside God.
Correction: The author clarifies that the term is used metaphorically when paired with God, just as 'two moons' refers to sun and moon without the sun being a moon alone.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is it permissible to call a servant 'khāliq' when paired with God?
A) Because the servant truly creates, just less perfectly.
B) Because of a metaphorical usage similar to calling the sun and moon 'two moons'.
C) Because the word 'khāliq' has multiple meanings.
D) Because the servant and God share the same power of creation.

Key Takeaway
The term 'khāliq' can be applied to servants only in a metaphorical compound sense, never as an independent attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the phrase 'the best of creators' (aḥsan al-khāliqīn), does your heart ever subtly entertain the idea that your own creative achievements are truly 'creation' independent of God? How does the clear distinction between fāʿil and khāliq in this passage expose that pride, and what will you do to root it out?
?
If you have ever felt uncomfortable calling God alone 'Creator' because of your own accomplishments, how does the linguistic principle of coupling—where a term is shared only when paired with God—reshape your understanding of dependence on Him? Will you commit to checking every attribution of 'creativity' in your life against this truth?
?
The author uses everyday analogies like 'the two Umars' and 'two moons' to explain a deep theological point. Is there any area of your faith where you have been tempted to over-analyze a phrase instead of accepting the simple, clear principle God has laid out? Will you submit your mind to the authority of this clear distinction and let it transform your worship?

Three Proofs of Exclusive Creative Power
Nasaﬁ enumerates three rational proofs against creation by other than Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational proofs (wujūh) that establish the impossibility of creative power for anyone other than Allah.

Core Idea
Only Allah can create; reason itself testifies to this impossibility.

Before diving into detailed scriptural analysis, Nasaﬁ lays out three concise rational arguments that immediately establish the conclusion. These proofs are the backbone of the entire discussion: they show that attributing creation to another leads to logical absurdity. Let's examine each argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once, then the English translation. Focus on the flow of the three proofs.
Notice the style: each proof is introduced briefly.
2
Identify each proof
The passage lists three 'wujūh' (aspects). Label them: 1) condition argument, 2) testimony of intellect, 3) implication of impossibility.
3
Understand the logic of proof three
Proof three argues that if creative power were possible for another, it would lead to an impossible consequence. Since truth cannot generate falsehood, the premise is impossible.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the role of intellect
Why does the author mention 'sound intellects' and 'consensus of opponents'? This shows the argument is universally compelling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إثبات قدرة التخليق لغير الله تعالى محال: الدليل على ذلك وجوه: أحدها فقد شرط ثبوت تلك القدرة وثبوت الشيء في حال انعدام شرطه الذي علق وجوده به محال تشهد العقول الصحيحة بفطرها بإحالته. والآخر: شهادة نفس العقل. والثالث: أن إثبات قدرة التخليق له يؤدي إلى أمر محال عرفت إحالته بإجماع الخصوم وشهادة العقول وما يؤدي إلى المحال يعرف إحالته لأن الصحيح لا ينتج الفاسد، والحق لا يولد الباطل. أما الأول فبيانه أن شرط ثبوت قدرة التخليق هو ثبوت العلم للخالق بالمخلوق قبل حصول المخلوق، ودليل كون ذلك شرطا كتاب الله تعالى ومساعدة الخصوم وشهادات المعارف، أما الكتاب فقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَسِرُّوا قَوْلَكُمْ أَوِ اجْهَرُوا بِهِ إِنَّهُ عَلِيمٌ بِذَاتِ الصُّدُورِ أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وَهُوَ اللَّطِيفُ الْخَبِيرُ﴾ فالآية تنص على أنه خالق أفعال العباد، وفيها أيضًا إشارة إلى أن كل خالق ينبغي أن يكون عالمًا بما خلق، أما كونها نصا فظاهر فإنه تعالى أخبر أنه يعلم ما يسر به العبد في قلبه وما يجهر به وقال: ﴿أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ﴾ وهو بيان أنه هو الخالق لأنه جعل كونه خالقا مقررا لما أخبر من تعلق علمه به كأنه قال: وهل يتصور أن لا يعلم من خلقه وأبدعه؟ ثم إنه تعالى جعل العلم بهذا ثابتا بثبوت تخليقه له، فكان هذا إخبارا بكونه مخلوقا له ثم بنى لثبوت العلم به على كونه مخلوقا له، ومثل هذا من أظهر ما يستدل به من النصوص. وأما الإشارة فلأنه أثبت علمه بما أسروا أو جهر بإثبات تخليقه لذلك، ولو جاز التخليق ممن لا علم له بما خلق لم يكن إثبات العلم بإثبات ما يجوز ثبوته بدون العلم حكمة، كمن يقول لآخر: أنا عالم بالفقه والكلام ثم يقول: ألا أعلم أنا ذلك وأنا ابن بزاز؟ أو يقول: وأنا طويل أو قصير أو وأنا عراقي أو حجازي أو يقول: ألا يعلم الفقه من هو بطل كمي أو جواد سخي؟ جل الله تعالى أن يثبت علمه بشيء بناء على ما لا يوجب له العلم به، ويجوز تعريه عن العلم فيكون في إثباته سفها مثبتا الشيء بما لا يجب ثبوته به كالذين يجهلون طرق إثبات الأشياء على منكري ثبوتها، فصح ما ادعينا من ثبوت العلم بالمخلوق شرطا لثبوت قدرة التخليق أو قرينة لها لا يزيلها بوجه من الوجوه في حال من الأحوال مع ما كانت الآية نصا في إثبات خلق أفعال العباد، فإذا أثبت الله تعالى قول أهل الحق لكتابه نصا
Establishing the power of creation (qudrat al-takhliq) for other than Allah the Exalted is impossible. The proof for that has aspects: One of them is that the condition for the existence of that power is the existence of the thing in a state of absence of its condition upon which its existence is conditioned – impossible, sound intellects witness its impossibility by their innate disposition. Another: the testimony of the intellect itself. Third: that establishing the power of creation for it leads to an impossible matter whose impossibility is known by consensus of the opponents and the testimony of intellects, and that which leads to the impossible is known to be impossible because the sound does not produce the corrupt, and the truth does not generate falsehood. As for the first, its explanation is that the condition for establishing the power of creation is the existence of knowledge for the creator of the created before the occurrence of the created. The proof that this is a condition is the Book of Allah the Exalted, the assistance of the opponents, and the testimonies of rational intuitions. As for the Book, His statement the Exalted: {And conceal your speech or publicize it; indeed, He is Knower of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know, while He is the Subtle, the Acquainted?} So the verse stipulates that He is the creator of the acts of servants, and in it also is an indication that every creator should be knowledgeable of what He created. As for its being a stipulation (naṣṣ), it is apparent, for He the Exalted informed that He knows what the servant conceals in his heart and what he publicizes, and He said: {Does He who created not know?} and it is a clarification that He is the Creator, because He made His being a creator a confirmation of what He informed of the attachment of His knowledge to it, as if He said: And can it be imagined that He does not know whom He created and originated? Then He the Exalted made knowledge of this established through the establishment of His creating it. So this was an informing that it is created by Him; then He built the establishment of knowledge of it upon its being created by Him. And such is among the most apparent things by which deduction is made from textual proofs. As for the indication, it is that He established His knowledge of what they concealed or publicized by establishing His creation of that. And if creation were permissible from one who has no knowledge of what he created, then the establishment of knowledge by establishing what is permissible to exist without knowledge would not be wisdom, like someone who says to another: 'I am knowledgeable of fiqh and kalām' then says: 'Do I not know that, while I am the son of a cloth merchant?' or says: 'And I am tall or short' or 'And I am Iraqi or Hijazi' or says: 'Does not know fiqh one who is a hero of Kam or a generous generous one?' Exalted is Allah from establishing His knowledge of something based on what does not necessitate knowledge of it, and it is permissible to be devoid of knowledge, so in establishing it there would be foolishness, establishing the thing by what does not necessitate its existence, like those who are ignorant of the methods of establishing things against deniers of their existence. So what we claimed is correct: that the existence of knowledge of the created is a condition for the existence of the power of creation, or a concomitant for it that no aspect can remove in any circumstance, along with the verse being a stipulation (naṣṣ) in establishing the creation of the acts of servants. So when Allah the Exalted establishes the statement of the people of truth for His Book as a stipulation (naṣṣ)...
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the impossibility of attributing creative power (qudrat al-takhliq) to any being other than Allah. The author presents three arguments (wujūh): First: The condition for the existence of such power is the existence of the thing (the creature) in a state where its condition is absent, which is impossible according to sound intellects. Second: The testimony of reason itself. Third: Attributing creative power to another leads to an impossibility recognized by consensus and reason, and what leads to impossibility is itself impossible, for sound does not produce corrupt and truth does not generate falsehood. The author then elaborates on the first argument: The condition for creative power is that the creator must have knowledge of the creature before bringing it into existence. Evidence for this condition is the Quran and rational agreement. The Quranic verse (Surah al-Mulk 13-14) is quoted to show that Allah is the creator of human acts and that He knows them, implying that a creator must know what He creates. The verse is both a direct stipulation and an indication. The author explains that the verse explicitly states that Allah knows what is hidden and public, and then asks 'Does He who created not know?' which confirms that He is the Creator. The indication is that knowledge is established by the act of creation; if creation were possible without knowledge, then establishing knowledge through creation would be futile, like claiming knowledge based on irrelevant attributes. Therefore, the condition stands: knowledge of the creature is necessary for creative power, and this condition cannot be removed in any case. The verse also establishes that Allah creates the acts of servants, affirming the position of Ahl al-Haqq.

Key Terms
قدرة التخليق
شرط
محال
عقول صحيحة
إجماع الخصوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that angels or prophets can create independently.
Correction: This passage proves that creative power is impossible for any other than Allah, as sound intellect and the impossibility of logical consequences demonstrate.

Checkpoint
According to the third proof, why is it impossible for creative power to belong to another being?
A) Because the Quran prohibits it.
B) Because opponents disagree.
C) Because it leads to an impossibility, and what leads to impossibility is impossible.
D) Because intellect cannot comprehend it.

Key Takeaway
The three rational proofs collectively show that ascribing creative power to anyone other than Allah is logically and rationally untenable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see something created — your own skills, a natural phenomenon, or a child’s birth — do you ever subconsciously attribute the act of creation to a secondary cause? What would it mean for your tawheed if that imputation were valid?
?
This lesson proves that only Allah can create. How does this truth change the way you view your daily efforts? Are you willing to stop claiming credit for outcomes and instead see them as direct acts of Allah's creative power? What would you need to give up to live that conviction?
?
The third proof says 'truth does not generate falsehood.' If you hold a belief that leads to an absurd conclusion, are you ready to abandon it even if it feels comfortable? What beliefs in your life might lead to spiritual contradiction, and are you willing to re-examine them now?

Divine Attributes

Condition of Knowledge for Creative Power
Nasaﬁ explains the first proof: condition of knowledge for creative power, with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why knowledge of the creature is a necessary condition for creative power, and how the Quranic verse 'Does He who created not know?' establishes this.

Core Idea
A creator must know what He creates; Allah alone meets this condition.

Nasaﬁ now elaborates the first argument from the previous lesson, explaining that the condition for creative power is prior knowledge of the creature. He supports this with a key Quranic verse and a rational analogy. Let's see how the verse proves both that Allah creates human acts and that He knows them.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic from 'أما الأول' to the end, then the translation. Notice the two parts: statement of condition, then evidence from Quran.
2
Identify the condition and its proof
The condition is knowledge before creation. The proofs are: Quran, agreement of opponents, and rational intuition. Focus on the Quranic proof.
3
Analyze the verse as 'nas' and 'ishara'
The verse is said to be a direct text (nas) that Allah creates acts, and an indication (ishara) that every creator must have knowledge.
The analogy about the cloth merchant clarifies why creation without knowledge is absurd.
4
Reflect on the analogy
The author uses an analogy: someone claims knowledge of fiqh based on being a cloth merchant's son. This is invalid. Similarly, establishing knowledge through creation is invalid if creation can occur without knowledge.
This shows wisdom in divine action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إثبات قدرة التخليق لغير الله تعالى محال: الدليل على ذلك وجوه: أحدها فقد شرط ثبوت تلك القدرة وثبوت الشيء في حال انعدام شرطه الذي علق وجوده به محال تشهد العقول الصحيحة بفطرها بإحالته. والآخر: شهادة نفس العقل. والثالث: أن إثبات قدرة التخليق له يؤدي إلى أمر محال عرفت إحالته بإجماع الخصوم وشهادة العقول وما يؤدي إلى المحال يعرف إحالته لأن الصحيح لا ينتج الفاسد، والحق لا يولد الباطل. أما الأول فبيانه أن شرط ثبوت قدرة التخليق هو ثبوت العلم للخالق بالمخلوق قبل حصول المخلوق، ودليل كون ذلك شرطا كتاب الله تعالى ومساعدة الخصوم وشهادات المعارف، أما الكتاب فقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَسِرُّوا قَوْلَكُمْ أَوِ اجْهَرُوا بِهِ إِنَّهُ عَلِيمٌ بِذَاتِ الصُّدُورِ أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وَهُوَ اللَّطِيفُ الْخَبِيرُ﴾ فالآية تنص على أنه خالق أفعال العباد، وفيها أيضًا إشارة إلى أن كل خالق ينبغي أن يكون عالمًا بما خلق، أما كونها نصا فظاهر فإنه تعالى أخبر أنه يعلم ما يسر به العبد في قلبه وما يجهر به وقال: ﴿أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ﴾ وهو بيان أنه هو الخالق لأنه جعل كونه خالقا مقررا لما أخبر من تعلق علمه به كأنه قال: وهل يتصور أن لا يعلم من خلقه وأبدعه؟ ثم إنه تعالى جعل العلم بهذا ثابتا بثبوت تخليقه له، فكان هذا إخبارا بكونه مخلوقا له ثم بنى لثبوت العلم به على كونه مخلوقا له، ومثل هذا من أظهر ما يستدل به من النصوص. وأما الإشارة فلأنه أثبت علمه بما أسروا أو جهر بإثبات تخليقه لذلك، ولو جاز التخليق ممن لا علم له بما خلق لم يكن إثبات العلم بإثبات ما يجوز ثبوته بدون العلم حكمة، كمن يقول لآخر: أنا عالم بالفقه والكلام ثم يقول: ألا أعلم أنا ذلك وأنا ابن بزاز؟ أو يقول: وأنا طويل أو قصير أو وأنا عراقي أو حجازي أو يقول: ألا يعلم الفقه من هو بطل كمي أو جواد سخي؟ جل الله تعالى أن يثبت علمه بشيء بناء على ما لا يوجب له العلم به، ويجوز تعريه عن العلم فيكون في إثباته سفها مثبتا الشيء بما لا يجب ثبوته به كالذين يجهلون طرق إثبات الأشياء على منكري ثبوتها، فصح ما ادعينا من ثبوت العلم بالمخلوق شرطا لثبوت قدرة التخليق أو قرينة لها لا يزيلها بوجه من الوجوه في حال من الأحوال مع ما كانت الآية نصا في إثبات خلق أفعال العباد، فإذا أثبت الله تعالى قول أهل الحق لكتابه نصا

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the impossibility of attributing creative power (qudrat al-takhliq) to any being other than Allah. The author presents three arguments (wujūh): First: The condition for the existence of such power is the existence of the thing (the creature) in a state where its condition is absent, which is impossible according to sound intellects. Second: The testimony of reason itself. Third: Attributing creative power to another leads to an impossibility recognized by consensus and reason, and what leads to impossibility is itself impossible, for sound does not produce corrupt and truth does not generate falsehood. The author then elaborates on the first argument: The condition for creative power is that the creator must have knowledge of the creature before bringing it into existence. Evidence for this condition is the Quran and rational agreement. The Quranic verse (Surah al-Mulk 13-14) is quoted to show that Allah is the creator of human acts and that He knows them, implying that a creator must know what He creates. The verse is both a direct stipulation and an indication. The author explains that the verse explicitly states that Allah knows what is hidden and public, and then asks 'Does He who created not know?' which confirms that He is the Creator. The indication is that knowledge is established by the act of creation; if creation were possible without knowledge, then establishing knowledge through creation would be futile, like claiming knowledge based on irrelevant attributes. Therefore, the condition stands: knowledge of the creature is necessary for creative power, and this condition cannot be removed in any case. The verse also establishes that Allah creates the acts of servants, affirming the position of Ahl al-Haqq.

Key Terms
شرط
علم
نص
إشارة
خلق أفعال العباد
حكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that human beings can create their own actions independently of Allah.
Correction: The passage proves that creative power requires knowledge of the creature before creation, which only Allah possesses, so human acts are created by Allah.

Checkpoint
What is the condition for creative power according to the first proof?
A) The creator must be visible.
B) The creator must have knowledge of the creature before creating.
C) The creator must be eternal.
D) The creator must be a human.

Key Takeaway
Creative power is impossible without prior knowledge, and only Allah possesses the perfect knowledge required for creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah did not know every detail of your life—every thought, every hidden deed—could He truly be called your Creator? What does that mean for how you live under His all-knowing gaze today?
?
The author says it would be foolish to claim knowledge based on something that could exist without it. Where in your own life have you assumed something about Allah without truly knowing Him from His revelation? What step will you take today to replace assumption with certain knowledge?
?
You act every day as if you have knowledge of what you are doing. But do you truly know the consequences of your actions as Allah does? How does your limited knowledge humble you, and how does it drive you to rely on the One whose knowledge is perfect?

Six Absurdities of Attributing Creative Power to Others
Imam Nasafi enumerates six absurdities resulting from attributing creative power to others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six rational absurdities that Imam Nasafi argues necessarily follow from ascribing creative power to any being other than Allah.

Core Idea
Attributing creative power to other than Allah unravels the very fabric of tawhid.

Imam Nasafi now presents a powerful argument by enumeration: if anyone other than Allah were to have creative power, it would lead to a cascade of logical absurdities that undermine the core principles of tawhid. This passage lists six such absurdities, each of which will be explained in detail later. As you read, notice how each builds on the impossibility of a second creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Focus on the overall claim and the list of six absurdities.
The author uses 'منها' to introduce each item.
2
Identify each absurdity
Go through the list one by one. For each, ask: what is the absurd consequence being described? Write them down in your own words.
There are six distinct points; make sure you catch all.
3
Reflect on their interconnectedness
Consider how these absurdities are not independent but mutually reinforcing. They all stem from the same root: dividing creative power.
For example, incapacitating Allah and invalidating proofs are related.
4
Understand the author's method
Notice that Nasafi uses 'adduced to absurdity' as a method to refute the claim. This is a common kalam technique.
The promise to explain each absurdity in detail shows this is an overview.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما دعوانا أن إثبات قدرة التخليق لغير الله تعالى يؤدي إلى المحال فدعوى صحيحة، وعند الكشف عن ذلك تبين أن ذلك يؤدي إلى ضروب من المحال منها: أنه يؤدي إلى القول بتعجيز الله تعالى أو كونه ممنوعًا. ومنها: أنه يؤدي إلى إبطال دلائل الموحدين على توحيد الصانع وتعجيز الموحدين عن إثبات وحدانية الصانع جل وعلا. ومنها: أن وجود محدث لم يوجده الله تعالى ولم يكن له عليه القدرة يؤدي إلى كون العالم بصانعين. ومنها: أنه يؤدي إلى أن تكون القدرة من صفات الفعل على مذاهب الخصوم، ويلزم على ذلك أنه لم يكن في الأزل قادرًا عندهم. ومنها: أنه يؤدي إلى وقوع التشابه بين فعل القديم والمحدث. ومنها: أنه يؤدي إلى جواز عبادة الله تعالى. ونبين كيفية كون كل من ذلك مؤديا إلى كل وجه من هذه الوجوه بعون الله وتوفيقه.
As for our claim that affirming creative power (qudrat al-takhlīq) for other than Allah the Exalted leads to absurdity, it is a correct claim. Upon investigation it becomes clear that it leads to kinds of absurdity: among them, that it leads to the statement of incapacitating Allah the Exalted or His being prevented. Among them, that it leads to invalidating the proofs of the monotheists for the oneness of the Maker and incapacitating the monotheists from establishing the oneness of the Maker, He being exalted and high. Among them, that the existence of an originated thing that Allah the Exalted did not originate and over which He has no power leads to the world having two makers. Among them, that it leads to power being among the attributes of action according to the doctrines of the opponents, and it follows from that that He was not powerful in pre-eternity according to them. Among them, that it leads to the occurrence of resemblance between the act of the Eternal and the originated. Among them, that it leads to the permissibility of worshipping Allah the Exalted. And we will explain how each of these leads to each of these aspects with the help of Allah and His granting success.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of six absurdities (ḍurūb min al-muḥāl) that follow from the thesis that someone other than Allah possesses creative power (qudrat al-takhlīq). The author states the claim that this thesis leads to absurdity is correct. He then lists six consequences: (1) it leads to saying that Allah is incapacitated or prevented; (2) it invalidates the proofs of monotheists for God's oneness and incapacitates them from proving it; (3) an originated thing not originated by Allah implies two makers; (4) it makes creative power an attribute of action, implying Allah was not powerful in pre-eternity; (5) it creates resemblance between the acts of the Eternal and originated; (6) it leads to the permissibility of worshiping Allah (probably a scribal error for worshiping other than Him, but remains). The author then promises to explain each of these in detail, with divine assistance.

Key Terms

تعجيز
منع
توحيد الصانع
صفات الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the six absurdities are independent and unrelated consequences, or that the list is exhaustive of all possible absurdities.
Correction: The six absurdities are interconnected and mutually reinforcing, all stemming from the same root: dividing creative power. The author does not claim the list is exhaustive; he presents 'kinds' (ḍurūb) of absurdity.

Key Takeaway
Attributing creative power to any other than Allah leads to multiple logical absurdities that collectively demolish the foundations of tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This passage says that attributing creative power to others 'incapacitates' Allah in your understanding. In what areas of your life—your work, relationships, or future plans—do you act as if your efforts are the ultimate cause, and how can you consciously depend on Allah as the sole creator of results?
?
The sixth absurdity is that believing others can create leads to worshipping them. Look at your heart: are there people, systems, or even yourself that you 'worship' by trusting them as the ultimate providers or fixers? What concrete step will you take today to redirect that trust exclusively to Allah?

The First Absurdity: God's Power Dependent on the Servant's Choice?
Nasafi proves the first absurdity and responds to an objection about God's power over opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi proof that if both God and servants create human actions, it leads to the absurdity of making God's power dependent on the servant's choice, and how the objection regarding God's power over opposites is answered.

Core Idea
Making God's power dependent on a servant's choice is impossible; but God's power over opposites is on a substitution basis.

Imam Nasafi presents the first absurdity against the view that both God and servants create human actions. He argues that if a servant could create an opposite to God's action, God's power would become contingent on the servant's refraining, which is impossible. Then he anticipates an objection: does this mean God cannot have power over opposites? He answers by clarifying that God's power is over each opposite on a substitution basis, not both simultaneously. This lesson walks through the argument and its defense.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the core argument
Identify how God's power becomes dependent on the servant's choice if both have creative power over opposites in the same subject.
The key phrase is 'فكانت قدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره موقوفة على امتناع العبد'.
3
Examine the objection
The opponents argue that the same logic would imply God cannot have power over opposites, because creating one prevents the other.
This is a common counterargument.
4
Analyze the response
Notice the clarification: God's power is over each opposite on a substitution basis (على البدل), not both simultaneously. The impossible is not under power.
This preserves God's omnipotence while avoiding absurdity.
5
Reflect on key terms
Review the terms تعجيز (incapacitation), منع (prevention), المتضادان (opposites), and على البدل (on a substitution basis).
These terms are central to the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الأول فإنا قلنا: إن ذلك يؤدي إلى تعجيز الباري جل وعلا فإن الباري لو كان قادرا على أن يخلق مثلاً في يد العبد حركة، والعبد قادر على أن يخلق فيه سكونًا ثم من المحال أن يوجد مقدور كل واحد منهما في المحل في وقت واحد لتضاد بين الحركة والسكون، وهذا لا نزاع فيه لعاقل، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فقد تعلق حينئذ ثبوت القدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره بامتناع العبد عن تحصيل مقدوره، ولو لم يمتنع عن تحصيل مقدوره لما ثبتت قدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره فكانت قدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره موقوفة على امتناع العبد عن تحصيل مقدور نفسه والعبد في الامتناع عن تحصيل مقدوره مختار إن شاء امتنع، وإن شاء لم يمتنع فصار مختارًا في إزالة قدرة الله تعالى إن شاء أزالها عن مقدوره، وإن شاء لم يزلها وإزالة القدرة تعجيز عندنا، وعندكم منع لجواز انضمام القدرة مع المنع عندكم، وكلا الأمرين أعني المنع أو التعجيز محال. فإن قالوا نلزمكم على هذا أن لا يكون الباري جل وعلا قادرا على المتضادين لأنه لو كان قادرًا عليهما ثم أوجد أحد المتضادين لصار معجزا ومانعا نفسه عن تحصيل ما يضاد لاستحالة قيام المتضادين في محل، وكما لا يجوز أن يكون الباري تعالى ممنوعًا أو معجزاً من قبل غيره لا يجوز أن يكون ممنوعا أو معجزا من قبل نفسه. قيل: إن الله تعالى قادر عندنا على كل واحد من المتضادين على البدل فيوصف بأنه قادر على إيجاد السكون في هذا المحل في هذه الحالة بدلاً عما أوجده فيه من الحركة وكذا على القلب، ولا يوصف بالقدرة بالمتضادين على الإطلاق لكون اجتماعهما محالاً، ولا دخول للمحال تحت القدرة، وبهذا لم يكن تعليق قدرته على مقدوره باختيار غيره بل هو القادر على أن يفعل أي المتضادين شاء وأي المتضادين خلق، خلق عن اختيار وعن أيهما امتنع، امتنع عن
As for the first, we said: that leads to incapacitating the Maker (al-Bārī), He being exalted and high. For if the Maker were able to create, for example, movement in the hand of the servant, and the servant were able to create in it rest, then it is impossible for the object of power of each of them to exist in the subject at one time due to the opposition between movement and rest, and there is no dispute about this among rational people. When the matter is so, then the establishment of the power of Allah the Exalted over His object of power becomes dependent upon the servant's refraining from effecting his object of power. And if he did not refrain from effecting his object of power, the power of Allah the Exalted over His object of power would not be established. Thus the power of Allah the Exalted over His object of power is suspended upon the servant's refraining from effecting his own object of power, and the servant in refraining from effecting his object of power is a chooser: if he wills he refrains, and if he wills he does not refrain. So he becomes a chooser in removing the power of Allah the Exalted: if he wills he removes it from His object of power, and if he wills he does not remove it. And removal of power is incapacitation (taʿjīz) with us, and with you it is prevention (manʿ) because of the permissibility of combining power with prevention according to you. Both matters, prevention or incapacitation, are impossible. And if they say: we object against you on this, that the Maker, exalted and high, would not be powerful over opposites (al-mutaḍādayn), because if He were powerful over them and then He brought one of the opposites into existence, He would become incapacitated and a preventer of Himself from effecting what is opposite, due to the impossibility of the simultaneous existence of opposites in a subject. And just as it is not permissible for the Maker to be prevented or incapacitated by another, it is not permissible for Him to be prevented or incapacitated by Himself. It is said: Allah the Exalted is powerful with us over each one of the opposites on a substitution basis (ʿalā al-badal). So He is described as being able to bring about rest in this subject in this state instead of what He brought about in it of movement, and likewise on reversal. And He is not described as having power over opposites absolutely, because their simultaneous existence is impossible, and the impossible does not fall under power. And by this, His power over His object of power is not dependent on the choice of another. Rather, He is the one who is able to do whichever of the opposites He wills, and whichever of the opposites He creates, He creates by choice, and from whichever He refrains, He refrains from
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a detailed proof of the first absurdity listed earlier, followed by an objection and its response. The author argues that if both God and a servant had creative power over contradictory things (e.g., movement and rest in the same hand), God's power would become dependent on the servant's choice, leading to God being either incapacitated (taʿjīz) or prevented (manʿ), both impossible. The opponents object that the same reasoning would apply to God's own power over opposites: if God is powerful over opposites (e.g., movement and rest), then creating one would make Him incapable of creating the other, thus self-incapacitation. The author responds by clarifying that God's power is over each opposite on a substitution basis (ʿalā al-badal), not both simultaneously. God is described as able to create movement or rest at will, but not both at once; the impossible does not fall under power. Thus God's power is not dependent on another's choice. The argument ends abruptly but completes the defense.

Key Terms

منع
المتضادان
على البدل
دخول المحال تحت القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's power over opposites means He can create both simultaneously, or the objection proves a defect in God.
Correction: God is powerful over each opposite individually on a substitution basis; simultaneous existence is impossible and thus not under power.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi's response, how is God powerful over opposites?
A) Simultaneously
B) On a substitution basis
C) Not at all
D) Through intermediaries

Key Takeaway
God's power over opposites is on a substitution basis; He is powerful over each individually, and the impossible does not fall under His power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's power were truly dependent on my choices, I would be the ultimate controller of my destiny. How deeply do I actually believe that God's power is absolute and not contingent on anyone's actions — and what in my life betrays a stance of trying to control outcomes as if God's power were waiting on me?
?
The objection that God cannot have power over opposites is refuted simply: He has power over each on substitution. Do I secretly harbor resentments against God's decrees because I feel He could have done differently, not accepting that His choice is perfect? What specific decree do I need to submit to today as the best possible alternative?
?
This lesson argues that the impossible does not fall under God's power. In my daily life, do I waste energy demanding or expecting the impossible from God — perhaps wanting a trial removed without wisdom, or a miracle that bypasses means? What one impossible thing am I clinging to that I need to release, trusting that God's power is already at work in the best possible way?

God's Power Over Opposites on Substitution Basis
Nasafi answers objection that God's power depends on human abstention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi theologians explain God's power over opposites without implying dependency or limitation.

Core Idea
God's power over opposites is on substitution, not simultaneity.

You are about to read a key passage from Nasafi's Tabṣirat al-Adilla. It addresses a common objection: if God's power over an action depends on a human not doing it, doesn't that make God's power dependent on human choice? The objection pushes to an absurdity, and Nasafi answers by clarifying the nature of God's power over opposites. This is a masterclass in precise theological reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the objection from the opponent starting at 'If they say: We hold against you...' until '...it is not permissible for Him to be prevented or incapacitated by Himself.' Understand the logical thrust: that God would be self-incapacitated if He were powerful over opposites.
Notice the opponent uses the terms 'incapacitated' (ta'jiz) and 'prevented' (man').
2
Identify Nasafi's answer
Look for the key phrase 'on a substitution basis' (badal). This is the core of the response. Nasafi says God is powerful over each opposite on a substitution basis, meaning He can choose to bring one into existence instead of the other.
3
See how this avoids dependency
Notice that Nasafi emphasizes that God's power is not dependent on human abstention. Rather, God's refraining from creating the opposite is by His own choice, not due to any prevention from Himself or another.
This addresses the original objection that God's power would depend on the servant's abstention.
4
Grasp the sign of perfection
Read the concluding sentence: 'And this is a sign of perfection of power.' Understand that being able to choose which opposite to create, and refraining by choice, indicates complete power, not limitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لتضاد بين الحركة والسكون ، وهذا لا نزاع فيه لعاقل، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فقد تعلق حينئذ ثبوت القدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره بامتناع العبد عن تحصيل مقدوره، ولو لم يمتنع عن تحصيل مقدوره لما ثبتت قدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره فكانت قدرة الله تعالى على مقدوره موقوفة على امتناع العبد عن تحصیل مقدور نفسه والعبد في الامتناع عن تحصيل مقدوره مختار إن شاء امتنع، وإن شاء لم يمتنع فصار مختارًا في إزالة قدرة الله تعالى إن شاء أزالها عن مقدوره، وإن شاء لم يزلها وإزالة القدرة تعجيز عندنا، وعندكم منع لجواز انضمام القدرة مع المنع عندكم ، وكلا الأمرين أعني المنع أو التعجيز محال. فإن قالوا نلزمكم على هذا أن لا يكون الباري جل وعلا قادرا على المتضادين لأنه لو كان قادرًا عليهما ثم أوجد أحد المتضادين لصار معجزا ومانعا نفسه عن تحصيل ما يضاد لاستحالة قيام المتضادين في محل، وكما لا يجوز أن يكون الباري تعالى ممنوعًا أو معجزاً من قبل غيره لا يجوز أن يكون ممنوعا أو معجزا من قبل نفسه. قيل: إن الله تعالى قادر عندنا على كل واحد من المتضادين على البدل فيوصف بأنه قادر على إيجاد السكون في هذا المحل في هذه الحالة بدلاً عما أوجده فيه من الحركة وكذا على القلب، ولا يوصف بالقدرة بالمتضادين على الإطلاق لكون اجتماعهما محالاً، ولا دخول للمحال تحت القدرة، وبهذا لم يكن تعليق قدرته على مقدوره باختيار غيره بل هو القادر على أن يفعل أي المتضادين شاء وأي المتضادين خلق، خلق عن اختيار وعن أيهما امتنع، امتنع عن اختيار لا بمنع من قبل نفسه أو من قبل غيره وهو أمارة كمال القدرة
Due to the opposition between motion and rest, and this is indisputable for any rational person. If this is the case, then the affirmation of the power of God Almighty over His object of power becomes dependent on the servant's refraining from acquiring his own object of power. And if he did not refrain from acquiring his object of power, the power of God Almighty over His object of power would not be established. So the power of God Almighty over His object of power is dependent on the servant's refraining from acquiring his own object of power. The servant, in refraining from acquiring his object of power, is a chooser: if he wills he refrains, and if he wills he does not refrain. Thus he becomes a chooser in removing God's power: if he wills he removes it from His object of power, and if he wills he does not remove it. Removing power is incapacitation (ta'jiz) according to us, and according to you it is prevention (man') due to the permissibility of power combining with prevention according to you. Both matters, I mean prevention or incapacitation, are impossible. If they say: 'We hold against you on this that the Creator, may He be exalted, would not be powerful over opposites, because if He were powerful over them and then brought one of the two opposites into existence, He would become incapacitated and a preventer of Himself from bringing into existence what opposes it, due to the impossibility of two opposites subsisting in a locus. And just as it is not permissible for the Exalted Creator to be prevented or incapacitated by another, it is not permissible for Him to be prevented or incapacitated by Himself.' It is said: Indeed, God Almighty is powerful according to us over each one of the opposites on a substitution basis (badal). So He is described as being powerful to bring about rest in this locus in this state instead of what He brought into existence therein of motion, and likewise for reversal. He is not described as having power over the two opposites absolutely, because their conjunction is impossible, and the impossible does not fall under power. By this, His power over His object of power is not dependent on the choice of another. Rather, He is powerful to do whichever of the two opposites He wills, and whichever of the two opposites He creates, He creates by choice, and whichever of them He refrains from, He refrains by choice, not due to prevention from Himself or from another. And this is a sign of perfection of power.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage contains an objection-and-answer unit. It begins by stating the Maturidi position that God's power over a specific object is contingent upon the human agent refraining from acquiring that same object. This sets up a potential problem: does this mean God's power depends on human choice? The objector argues that this leads to an absurdity: if God were powerful over two opposites (e.g., motion and rest), then when He creates one, He would be prevented or incapacitated from creating the other, which would imply a limitation on God, either from another or from Himself, both of which are impossible. The answer clarifies that God's power over opposites is not simultaneous but on a substitution basis (badal). He is powerful to create either one at His choice, but since their conjunction is impossible, He is not described as having power over both absolutely. Therefore, His power is not dependent on human abstention; rather, His refraining from the opposite is by His own choice, not due to any prevention. This actually indicates the perfection of His power, not a defect.

Key Terms
قدرة
متضادين
بدل
تعجيز
منع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think God's inability to create both opposites simultaneously indicates a limitation in His power.
Correction: Nasafi explains that creating both opposites is impossible (not an object of power), and God's power over each on a substitution basis and His choice to refrain show perfection, not limitation.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi's answer, how is God described as powerful over two opposites?
A) He is powerful over both simultaneously.
B) He is powerful over each one on a substitution basis.
C) He is powerful over one and not the other.
D) He is not powerful over opposites at all.

Key Takeaway
God's power over opposites is on a substitution basis, meaning He can create either at His choice, and this demonstrates perfection and independence of His power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation where you feel trapped between two sinful choices, do you truly believe that God has the power to guide you to the right one without being limited by your own inclinations? How does the truth that God's power is exercised by choice, not by force, change your reliance on Him in that moment?
?
The passage refutes the idea that human abstention enables God's power. In your life, have you ever excused your lack of obedience by saying 'God didn't give me the strength' or 'I'm just too weak'? How does the lesson that God's refraining is by His own choice—and that He can empower you if He wills—confront that excuse?
?
God's perfection includes power over each opposite on substitution. Is there an area of your life where you have been assuming God cannot or will not change you because you think the opposite is stronger? Will you let this understanding of God's complete authority push you to ask Him for the impossible change today?

The Sign of Perfect Power
Definition of true power and refutation of prevention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how true divine power is defined and why human acquisition cannot be a sign of incapacity in God.

Core Idea
True power is voluntary and unimpeded; kasb does not hinder it.

The author begins by distinguishing genuine power from its opposite. He defines true power as ability that is not blocked by any internal or external obstacle. Then he shows that the Mu'tazilite claim—that human kasb could prevent God from acting—would actually indicate divine weakness, which is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic definition of power
Read the first sentence which defines true power as choice not prevented by oneself or others. This sets the criterion for evaluating the argument.
Note the term 'ikhtiyār' (choice) as central.
2
Understand the Mu'tazilite claim
The author quotes the opposing view: 'he is able to obtain his object of power if others did not prevent him.' Recognize this as a flawed understanding of divine power.
3
See the conclusion
The author concludes that if God were prevented by the servant's kasb, that would be a sign of incapacity. But true power is the opposite: it is not subject to such prevention.
This refutes the idea that kasb limits God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اختيار لا بمنع من قبل نفسه أو من قبل غيره وهو أمارة كمال القدرة، وفيما زعموا هو قادر على تحصيل مقدوره لو لم يمنعه غيره عن ذلك أو لم يعجزه، ويمتنع عن تحصيل مقدوره بمنع العبد إياه لا باختياره، وهذا هو أمارة العجز والقهر والمنع، ومثل هذا التعجيز أو المنع لا يلزمه بإثبات قدرة العبد على الكسب لأن كسبه مقدور الله تعالى، والله تعالى هو الموجد له فلا يكون في اشتغاله بالكسب إزالة قدرة الله تعالى عن مقدوره ليلزم التعجيز أو المنع بخلاف إثبات قدرة التخليق على ما قررنا. والذي يؤيد ما ذكرنا أن كل فعل من أفعال العبد عرض وهو قبل حدوثه وخروجه من العدم إلى الوجود كان معلوم الباري جل وعلا بلا خوف، وهو عندهم جميعًا شيء، وعند البصريين منهم عوض، وعند الجبائي إن كان عند الوجد حركة فهو في حال العدم أيضا حركة، ثم لا شك أن في حال عدمه معلوم الله تعالى، والله تعالى يعلمه شيئا في حال عدمه، وعندهم وعند البصريين يعلمه عرضا وعند الجبائي منهم يعلمه حركة. ثم الحال لا يخلو إما إن كانت لله تعالى عليه قدرة كما للعبد عليه قدرة ويصح من كل واحد منهما الانفراد بإيجاده كما هو مذهب طائفة منهم، وإما إن كانت قدرة الله تعالى غير متيقنة لما كان مقدورًا للعبد لاستحالة كون مقدور لقادرين كما هو مذهب جمهورهم، ولا وجه إلى هذا ؛ لأن الله تعالى هو الذي يتولى إعطاء العبد قدرة الفعل وهو المقدر له، ومن المحال أن يقدر ذات ما غيره على ما لا قدرة للمقدر عليه، ولو جاز ذا لجاز أن يقدر المقعد غيره على عين المشي الذي المقعد عنه عاجز وهو محال، وكذا من المحال أن يعلم ذات غيره شيئًا لم يكن ذلك الشيء معلومًا لهذا العلم من غير فصل بين القديم والمحدث، فكذا هذا، وإحالة هذا مما تعرفه العوام ببدائههم وأوائل عقولهم حتى لو صور لأغبى خليقة الله تعالى من العوام قول المعتزلة في تجويز تخليق الله تعالى القدرة للعبد على ما لا يقدر الله تعالى عليه بنفسه أو يقدر أحد من العباد إقدار ذات ما على ما لا يقدر عليه الذات المقدر، لتسارعوا إلى تسفيه القائل له الراضى بذلك مذهبًا لنفسه، كما يعرفون إحالة تعليم ذات ما ذاتاً ما لا علم لا للمعلم به، ويتسارعون إلى تسفيه المجوز لذلك وذلك محال، وخروج عن قضية البداهة وأوائل العقول فكذا هذا، ألا ترى أن القول بتخليق قدرة ممن ليس بقادر عليها محال كما أن القول بتخليق علم ممن ليس بعالم به محال فكذا القول بتخليق قدرة على فعل ممن ليس بقادر على ذلك الفعل يكون محالاً كالقول بتخليق علم بمعلوم ممن ليس بعالم بذلك المعلوم.
Choice not by prevention from himself or from others, and it is a sign of perfection of power. And in what they claim, he is able to obtain his object of power if others did not prevent him from that or incapacitate him, and he refrains from obtaining his object of power by the servant's prevention of him, not by his choice, and this is a sign of incapacity, coercion, and prevention. And such incapacitation or prevention is not necessitated by affirming the servant's power over acquisition (al-kasb) because his acquisition is an object of power of God Most High, and God Most High is the one who brings it into existence, so there is not in his occupation with acquisition any removal of God's power over His object of power to necessitate incapacitation or prevention, unlike affirming creative power (qudrat al-takhlīq) as we have established. And what supports what we have mentioned is that every action of the servant is an accident, and before its occurrence and its emergence from non-existence to existence it was known to the Creator, Glorified and Exalted, without dispute. And it is, according to all of them, a thing; and according to the Basrans among them, an accident; and according to al-Jubba'i, if it is a movement when found, then in the state of non-existence it is also a movement. Then there is no doubt that in the state of its non-existence it is known to God Most High, and God Most High knows it as a thing in the state of its non-existence. And according to them and according to the Basrans, He knows it as an accident, and according to al-Jubba'i among them, He knows it as a movement. Then the case is not free: either God Most High has power over it just as the servant has power over it, and it is valid for each one of them to bring it about individually, as is the doctrine of a group of them; or God's power is not certain over what is an object of power of the servant due to the impossibility of an object of power for two able ones, as is the doctrine of the majority of them. And there is no way to this, because God Most High is the one who undertakes giving the servant the power of the act, and He is the one who enables him. And it is impossible for one being to enable another over what the enabler has no power over. And if this were permissible, it would be permissible for the crippled to enable another over the very walking that the crippled is incapable of, which is impossible. And likewise, it is impossible for one being to teach another something that was not known to that teacher, without distinction between the eternal and the temporal. So this is likewise. And the impossibility of this is known by the common people through their innate intuitions and first principles of their intellects, so much so that if one were to present to the stupidest of God's creation among the common people the statement of the Mu'tazila permitting God's creation of power for the servant over what God Himself has no power over, or any of the servants enabling a being over what that being cannot do, they would hasten to deem the speaker foolish, who is content with that as a doctrine for himself, just as they know the impossibility of a being teaching another what the teacher has no knowledge of, and they hasten to deem foolish the one who permits that. And that is impossible and a departure from the dictate of innate intuition and first principles of intellects. So this is likewise. Do you not see that the statement about creating power from one who has no power over it is impossible, just as the statement about creating knowledge from one who has no knowledge of it is impossible? So likewise, the statement about creating power over an act from one who has no power over that act is impossible, like the statement about creating knowledge of a known thing from one who has no knowledge of that known thing.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is an extended argument proving that the human power of acquisition (al-kasb) does not restrict or limit divine power. The author begins by defining true power (qudra): a voluntary ability unimpeded by internal or external obstacles. If the servant's power could prevent God from acting, that would indicate divine incapacity, which is impossible. The author then clarifies that the servant's acquisition is itself created by God, so exercising kasb does not remove anything from God's power. Next, the author supports this with the premise that all human actions are accidents known to God before they exist. Different Mu'tazilite schools (Basrans, al-Jubba'i) disagree on whether such actions are 'things' or specific types of accidents like movements. The author then presents a dilemma: either both God and the servant have independent power over the same act (the view of some Mu'tazila), or God's power is not involved because the act belongs exclusively to the servant (majority view). Both are false: the first would be impossible because no act can have two independent agents; the second fails because God is the giver of all power. The author uses analogies: a crippled person cannot enable another to walk, just as one who lacks knowledge cannot teach. These impossibilities are evident to common sense, so the Mu'tazilite claim that God gives the servant power over what God Himself cannot do is absurd. The passage concludes by drawing a parallel between creating power and creating knowledge: just as God cannot create knowledge in another of something He does not know, He cannot create power over an act He cannot perform.

Key Terms
قدرة
كسب
اختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that human free choice competes with divine power, so God cannot act fully.
Correction: True divine power is not subject to prevention from any creature; kasb is itself created by God, so it does not limit Him.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does it mean if God is prevented from acting by the servant's kasb?
A) It shows God's power is perfect.
B) It shows God's power is limited.
C) It shows God chooses to be prevented.
D) It shows God's power is infinite.

Key Takeaway
True divine power is voluntary and unimpeded; kasb cannot cause prevention because that would imply imperfection in God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own repeated sins, do you ever comfort yourself by thinking, 'God could have prevented me, but He didn't'? How does this passage challenge that excuse? What does it reveal about your heart's attitude toward divine power?
?
The Mu'tazilites argued that human kasb prevents God's act to preserve human responsibility. Are you tempted to believe that your choices somehow limit God's sovereignty? How does this passage call you to trust in God's perfect power even over your own actions?
?
If God's power is truly unimpeded, what does that mean for your fears about the future? What worry are you holding onto as if God could be prevented from working? Will you surrender it now to the One whose power is perfect?

Actions Known as Accidents Before Existence
Premise that actions are known accidents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that human actions are accidents known to God before they exist, supporting the idea that kasb is within God's power.

Core Idea
All human acts are accidents known to God from eternity.

The author now strengthens his argument by pointing out that every human action is an accident ('arad) that was known to God before it came into existence. Even among the Mu'tazilites, there is agreement that these actions are 'things' or specific types like movements. This shows that God's knowledge encompasses all acts, so His power is not restricted by their occurrence.

Guided Path
1
Read the premise about accidents
Read the statement that every servant's action is an accident, known to God before its occurrence. This is a foundational premise in kalam.
Accidents are temporary, created attributes.
2
Note the Mu'tazilite variations
Observe the differences: Basrans call it an accident (arad), al-Jubba'i calls a movement a movement even when non-existent. The point is that it is known to God.
This shows internal diversity but agreement on pre-existence knowledge.
3
Connect to divine power
The fact that God knows the act before it exists implies that it is within His knowledge and thus within His power. Kasb does not surprise God.

The Impossibility of Two Co-Agents
Refutation of two independent powers and common sense argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is impossible for both God and the servant to have independent power over the same act, and why the Mu'tazilite view leads to absurdity.

Core Idea
No act can have two independent agents; God is the sole creator.

The author now presents a dilemma regarding the relationship between divine power and human power over the same action. Either both have power (but then two agents for one act is impossible) or only the servant has power (but God is the giver of all power). Using analogies of a cripple enabling walking and a teacher teaching what he doesn't know, the author demonstrates the absurdity of the Mu'tazilite position. Finally, he appeals to common sense to confirm the conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dilemma
Read the two options: either both God and servant have power over the act, or God's power is not certain. Understand why both are false.
The first option is the view of a group, the second of the majority.
2
Analyze the first refutation
The author argues God gives the servant power; it's impossible for the enabler (God) to be unable to do what He enables another to do. Analogy: a cripple cannot enable walking.
3
Analyze the second refutation
Similarly, one cannot teach what one doesn't know. God cannot create power for an act He cannot perform.
4
Consider the common sense appeal
The author says even the common people would deem such a view foolish. This reinforces the logical conclusion.
The parallel between power and knowledge is emphasized.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أمارة العجز والقهر والمنع، ومثل هذا التعجيز أو المنع لا يلزمه بإثبات قدرة العبد على الكسب لأن كسبه مقدور الله تعالى، والله تعالى هو الموجد له فلا يكون في اشتغاله بالكسب إزالة قدرة الله تعالى عن مقدوره ليلزم التعجيز أو المنع بخلاف إثبات قدرة التخليق على ما قررنا. والذي يؤيد ما ذكرنا أن كل فعل من أفعال العبد عرض وهو قبل حدوثه وخروجه من العدم إلى الوجود كان معلوم الباري جل وعلا بلا خوف، وهو عندهم جميعًا شيء، وعند البصريين منهم عوض، وعند الجبائي إن كان عند الوجد حركة فهو في حال العدم أيضا حركة، ثم لا شك أن في حال عدمه معلوم الله تعالى، والله تعالى يعلمه شيئا في حال عدمه، وعندهم وعند البصريين يعلمه عرضا وعند الجبائي منهم يعلمه حركة. ثم الحال لا يخلو إما إن كانت لله تعالى عليه قدرة كما للعبد عليه قدرة ويصح من كل واحد منهما الانفراد بإيجاده كما هو مذهب طائفة منهم، وإما إن كانت قدرة الله تعالى غير متيقنة لما كان مقدورًا للعبد لاستحالة كون مقدور لقادرين كما هو مذهب جمهورهم، ولا وجه إلى هذا ؛ لأن الله تعالى هو الذي يتولى إعطاء العبد قدرة الفعل وهو المقدر له، ومن المحال أن يقدر ذات ما غيره على ما لا قدرة للمقدر عليه، ولو جاز ذا لجاز أن يقدر المقعد غيره على عين المشي الذي المقعد عنه عاجز وهو محال، وكذا من المحال أن يعلم ذات غيره شيئًا لم يكن ذلك الشيء معلومًا لهذا العلم من غير فصل بين القديم والمحدث، فكذا هذا، وإحالة هذا مما تعرفه العوام ببدائههم وأوائل عقولهم حتى لو صور لأغبى خليقة الله تعالى من العوام قول المعتزلة في تجويز تخليق الله تعالى القدرة للعبد على ما لا يقدر الله تعالى عليه بنفسه أو يقدر أحد من العباد إقدار ذات ما على ما لا يقدر عليه الذات المقدر، لتسارعوا إلى تسفيه القائل له الراضى بذلك مذهبًا لنفسه، كما يعرفون إحالة تعليم ذات ما ذاتاً ما لا علم لا للمعلم به، ويتسارعون إلى تسفيه المجوز لذلك وذلك محال، وخروج عن قضية البداهة وأوائل العقول فكذا هذا، ألا ترى أن القول بتخليق قدرة ممن ليس بقادر عليها محال كما أن القول بتخليق علم ممن ليس بعالم به محال فكذا القول بتخليق قدرة على فعل ممن ليس بقادر على ذلك الفعل يكون محالاً كالقول بتخليق علم بمعلوم ممن ليس بعالم بذلك المعلوم.
Choice not by prevention from himself or from others, and it is a sign of perfection of power. And in what they claim, he is able to obtain his object of power if others did not prevent him from that or incapacitate him, and he refrains from obtaining his object of power by the servant's prevention of him, not by his choice, and this is a sign of incapacity, coercion, and prevention. And such incapacitation or prevention is not necessitated by affirming the servant's power over acquisition (al-kasb) because his acquisition is an object of power of God Most High, and God Most High is the one who brings it into existence, so there is not in his occupation with acquisition any removal of God's power over His object of power to necessitate incapacitation or prevention, unlike affirming creative power (qudrat al-takhlīq) as we have established. And what supports what we have mentioned is that every action of the servant is an accident, and before its occurrence and its emergence from non-existence to existence it was known to the Creator, Glorified and Exalted, without dispute. And it is, according to all of them, a thing; and according to the Basrans among them, an accident; and according to al-Jubba'i, if it is a movement when found, then in the state of non-existence it is also a movement. Then there is no doubt that in the state of its non-existence it is known to God Most High, and God Most High knows it as a thing in the state of its non-existence. And according to them and according to the Basrans, He knows it as an accident, and according to al-Jubba'i among them, He knows it as a movement. Then the case is not free: either God Most High has power over it just as the servant has power over it, and it is valid for each one of them to bring it about individually, as is the doctrine of a group of them; or God's power is not certain over what is an object of power of the servant due to the impossibility of an object of power for two able ones, as is the doctrine of the majority of them. And there is no way to this, because God Most High is the one who undertakes giving the servant the power of the act, and He is the one who enables him. And it is impossible for one being to enable another over what the enabler has no power over. And if this were permissible, it would be permissible for the crippled to enable another over the very walking that the crippled is incapable of, which is impossible. And likewise, it is impossible for one being to teach another something that was not known to that teacher, without distinction between the eternal and the temporal. So this is likewise. And the impossibility of this is known by the common people through their innate intuitions and first principles of their intellects, so much so that if one were to present to the stupidest of God's creation among the common people the statement of the Mu'tazila permitting God's creation of power for the servant over what God Himself has no power over, or any of the servants enabling a being over what that being cannot do, they would hasten to deem the speaker foolish, who is content with that as a doctrine for himself, just as they know the impossibility of a being teaching another what the teacher has no knowledge of, and they hasten to deem foolish the one who permits that. And that is impossible and a departure from the dictate of innate intuition and first principles of intellects. So this is likewise. Do you not see that the statement about creating power from one who has no power over it is impossible, just as the statement about creating knowledge from one who has no knowledge of it is impossible? So likewise, the statement about creating power over an act from one who has no power over that act is impossible, like the statement about creating knowledge of a known thing from one who has no knowledge of that known thing.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is an extended argument proving that the human power of acquisition (al-kasb) does not restrict or limit divine power. The author begins by defining true power (qudra): a voluntary ability unimpeded by internal or external obstacles. If the servant's power could prevent God from acting, that would indicate divine incapacity, which is impossible. The author then clarifies that the servant's acquisition is itself created by God, so exercising kasb does not remove anything from God's power. Next, the author supports this with the premise that all human actions are accidents known to God before they exist. Different Mu'tazilite schools (Basrans, al-Jubba'i) disagree on whether such actions are 'things' or specific types of accidents like movements. The author then presents a dilemma: either both God and the servant have independent power over the same act (the view of some Mu'tazila), or God's power is not involved because the act belongs exclusively to the servant (majority view). Both are false: the first would be impossible because no act can have two independent agents; the second fails because God is the giver of all power. The author uses analogies: a crippled person cannot enable another to walk, just as one who lacks knowledge cannot teach. These impossibilities are evident to common sense, so the Mu'tazilite claim that God gives the servant power over what God Himself cannot do is absurd. The passage concludes by drawing a parallel between creating power and creating knowledge: just as God cannot create knowledge in another of something He does not know, He cannot create power over an act He cannot perform.

Key Terms
قدرة
تخليق
تعجيز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some Mu'tazilites thought that both God and the servant can be agents of the same act, or that God can give power for acts He cannot do.
Correction: No act can have two independent agents, and God cannot give power for what He cannot do, as that would imply imperfection.

Checkpoint
What analogy does the author use to show the impossibility of God creating power for an act He cannot perform?
A) A rich person giving money he doesn't have.
B) A crippled person enabling another to walk.
C) A blind person teaching someone to see.
D) A parent teaching a child.

Key Takeaway
It is impossible for God to enable the servant over what God cannot do, and common sense confirms this.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the analogy of the crippled man enabling another to walk. In your own life, are there areas where you rely on your own ability without recognizing that God is the One who truly enables you? How can you shift your mindset to see every act as a gift from His power, not your own?
?
The author says even the stupidest person would find the Mu'tazila view ridiculous. Is there a belief you hold about God that, if you tested it against your innate intuition (fitra), you would find inconsistent? What would it mean to trust your God-given reason in matters of faith?
?
If God cannot give you power to do what He Himself cannot do, what does this imply about the nature of your actions? Do you truly believe that every good deed you do is only possible because God is capable of it? How does that affect your gratitude and humility?

God Cannot Create Power for What He Does Not Will
First Mu'tazilite objection and Maturidi response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi response to the Mu'tazilite analogy between power and will is based on the comprehensiveness of God's will.

Core Idea
God's will covers all things, so He cannot create a will for what He does not will.

This lesson examines the first of two Mu'tazilite objections against the Maturidi doctrine of divine attributes. The objection attempts to draw an analogy between will and power, but the Maturidi response shows a critical difference rooted in the universal scope of God's will. By understanding this response, you will see how kalam arguments require precise attention to each attribute's unique implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the logical flow from objection to answer.
The objection uses an analogy: if God can create will without willing, why not power without having power?
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite analogy
The Mu'tazilites argue by analogy that what is permissible for will should be permissible for power. Identify both sides of the analogy.
3
Understand the Maturidi refutation
The author rejects the analogy because God's will is comprehensive over all temporal things. Therefore, there is no act for which God is not willing, so the analogy fails.
The comprehensiveness of God's will (عموم الإرادة) is a key Maturidi doctrine.
4
Note the charge of corrupt principle
The author concludes that the objection is built on a corrupt principle (أصل فاسد). Consider what that principle might be.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: لما جاز أن يخلق الباري جل جلاله إرادة الفعل لا يكون هذا مريدًا له، فلم لا يجوز أن يخلق قدرة على فعل لا قدرة له عليه؟ قيل: عندنا لا فرق بين هذا وبين ما ألزمنا، فإن الله تعالى كما يستحيل أن يخلق قدرة لغيره على فعل لا قدرة له على ذلك الفعل يستحيل أن يخلق إرادة لغيره لفعل لا يكون هو مريدًا لذلك الفعل لما نبين بعد هذا أن من مذهبنا القول بعموم إرادة الله تعالى المحدثات، وهذا السؤال بنيتم على أصلكم الفاسد. فإن قالوا: القول بما قلتم يؤدي إلى أن يوجد من الله تعالى إرادة للمتضادين في محل واحد في وقت واحد، فإنه إذا خلق لذات ما إرادة لفعل في محل، وخلق لآخر إرادة ضد ذلك الفعل في عين ذلك المحل في تلك الساعة، وكان هو تعالى
For if they say: Since it is permissible for the Creator, may His Majesty be exalted, to create the will for an act without Himself being willing for it, why is it not permissible for Him to create power over an act without Himself having power over it? It is said: According to us, there is no difference between this and what we have required. For God Most High, just as it is impossible for Him to create power for another over an act that He has no power over, it is impossible for Him to create will for another for an act that He is not willing for, as we will explain after this that our doctrine includes the assertion of the comprehensiveness of God's will over temporal things. And this question is built upon your corrupt principle. For if they say: The statement you have made leads to the existence from God Most High of will for two opposites in one locus at one time, for if He creates for one being a will for an act in a locus, and creates for another a will for the opposite of that act in the same locus at that same hour, and He, Most High,
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes two objections raised by the Mu'tazilites. The first objection argues by analogy: if God can create a will (irāda) in a person without Himself being willing (murīd) for that act, then why cannot God create power (qudra) for a person without Himself having power over that act? The author responds by rejecting the analogy: according to Maturidi doctrine, God's will is universal and encompasses all temporal things, so it is impossible for God to create a will in another for something He does not will. The objection is based on a false principle (aṣl fāsid). The second objection claims that if God creates conflicting wills in different agents at the same time, this would entail that God wills both opposites simultaneously, which is impossible. The text breaks off before the full answer, but the implied response would likely deny that creating a will in another requires God's own will to be directly involved in that specific act, or that God's will is not contradictory because it relates to different agents in different ways. The incomplete passage highlights the ongoing dialectical engagement with Mu'tazilite arguments.

Key Terms
إرادة
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God can create an attribute in another, He must Himself possess that attribute in the same way.
Correction: The Maturidi position is that God's will is comprehensive, so He does will all acts, but He may not directly exercise power over them in the same sense.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the analogy that if God can create will without willing, He can create power without having power?
A) Because power and will are different kinds of attributes.
B) Because God's will is comprehensive over all temporal things, so He cannot create a will for something He does not will.
C) Because the analogy was proposed by heretics and is invalid.
D) Because the author believes God does not create wills in others at all.

Key Takeaway
The comprehensiveness of God's will (عموم الإرادة) is the foundational principle that refutes the Mu'tazilite analogy between power and will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's will covers every event in your life, including your rebellious moments, how does that reshape your view of repentance? Can you truly turn back to Him without acknowledging that even your turning is within His will?
?
The Mu'tazilites assumed a limitation on God's will based on their own reasoning. What assumptions do you hold that effectively limit God's sovereignty in your daily decisions? Are you willing to surrender those to the comprehensive will of God?
?
This passage shows that God cannot create in you a will for what He does not will. Does your heart's desires align with what you know God wills? If not, what step will you take today to seek alignment?

The Alleged Contradiction in God Wills Opposites
Second Mu'tazilite objection (incomplete)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second Mu'tazilite objection that God creating conflicting wills leads to Him willing opposites, and why the full Maturidi response requires further context.

Core Idea
Creating wills in others does not require God to Himself will those specific acts in a contradictory manner.

This lesson presents the second objection raised by the Mu'tazilites, which attempts to show that the Maturidi position leads to impossible consequences. The objection argues that if God creates conflicting wills in different agents, then He would be willing both opposites at once. However, the answer to this objection is cut off in the manuscript; we will examine the objection and consider how the Maturidi scholar might respond.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. The objection presents a scenario where God creates wills for opposite acts in the same locus at the same time.
2
Understand the logical problem
The Mu'tazilites claim that this scenario would imply that God wills both opposites simultaneously, which is impossible. Identify the consequence they draw.
3
Note the incomplete answer
The passage ends mid-sentence. The author's full response is not preserved here. Consider what the next words 'وكان هو تعالى' might introduce.
The expected response would likely deny that creating wills in creatures entails God's own will being contradictory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself in a situation where two people, both sincere in their faith, prayed for opposite outcomes? Does this passage challenge your assumption that only one of them could be aligned with God's will? How might understanding that God creates different wills in different people for a greater purpose change your posture toward those who disagree with you on important matters?
?
