Refutation of Similarity Between Divine and Human Acts
Nasafi refutes the objection that similarity of acts implies similarity of agents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that similarity between divine and human acts does not imply similarity between God and humans, because divine attributes (like knowledge) are fundamentally different.

Core Idea
Acts may appear similar, but divine and human knowledge differ fundamentally.

This passage addresses a crucial objection: if divine and human acts are both 'bringing into existence', then God and humans would be similar. Nasafi responds by focusing on the attribute of knowledge. He distinguishes eternal divine knowledge from temporal human knowledge, showing that similarity in act does not entail similarity in essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, paying close attention to the objector's claim that similarity of acts leads to similarity of agents.
The objector argues that if both acts are 'bringing into existence', then God and humans become similar in attributes like knowledge.
2
Identify Nasafi's two-part response
Notice how Nasafi first references the earlier distinction between involuntary (divine) and voluntary (human) acts, then focuses on knowledge: God's knowledge is eternal (azalī), while human knowledge is temporal (muḥdath).
3
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider why distinguishing the nature of knowledge is important: it prevents drawing false conclusions about God's essence based on superficial similarities.
This connects to the broader Māturīdī emphasis on God's transcendence (tanzīh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن عندهم قد يكون فعل الله تعالى ما هو ذلك وخضوع لأن خلق الله تعالى عندهم المخلوق، ولا شك أن كل مخلوق فيه ذلة وخضوع وحاجة، ومن المخلوقات ما هو شيطان وشر وفتنة وابتلاء وفساد ونتن وخبث وقذرة، وكل ذلك عندهم فعل الله تعالى، فأنى يصح ما ذكر من الفرق وإبطال التشابه بين خلق الله تعالى وبين خلق غيره؟! فإن قالوا: لو كان يقع الاشتباه بين فعلنا وفعل الله تعالى لأن كل واحد من الفعلين إخراج من العدم إلى الوجود وإحداث لكان الاشتباه بين الله وبين الخلق ثابتا لأنه تعالى عالم والعبد أيضا عالم. قيل له: هذا الكلام فاسد، فإن الكلام قد سبق أن حركة المرتعش وحركات العروق النابضة فعل الله تعالى عندهم والحركة الاختيارية فعل العبد، وبينهما متشابهه ولا يمكن إثبات مخالفة بينهما في ذاتيهما على ما قررنا. فأما الله تعالى فهو عالم بعلم أزلي والعبد عالم بعلم محدث، فلا يكون بين العالمين مشابهة، وعلى أصل النجارية المشتبهان مشتبهان بأنفسهما لا باشتباه هو
Indeed, according to them, the act of Allah the Exalted may be that which is humility, because the creation of Allah the Exalted is, according to them, the created being, and there is no doubt that every created being has lowliness and humility and need, and among created beings are what is satan, evil, trial, affliction, corruption, stench, filth, and impurity, and all of that according to them is the act of Allah the Exalted. So how can what was mentioned of the distinction and invalidation of similarity between the creation of Allah and the creation of others be correct? For if they say: If similarity occurs between our act and the act of Allah because each of the two acts is a bringing into existence from non-existence and an innovation, then similarity between Allah and creation would be established because He is knowing and the servant is also knowing. It is said to him: This speech is corrupt, for the discussion has already preceded that the movement of the tremulous and the movements of pulsating veins are the act of Allah according to them, and the voluntary movement is the act of the servant, and between them there is similarity and it is not possible to establish difference between them in their essences according to what we have established. As for Allah the Exalted, He is knowing with eternal knowledge, and the servant is knowing with temporal knowledge, so there is no similarity between the two knowers. And according to the principle of the Najjāriyya, the two similar things are similar by themselves, not by a similarity that is...
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is an objection and answer regarding the similarity between divine and human acts. The objector argues that if divine and human acts are considered similar because both involve creation ex nihilo, then God and humans would be similar in attributes like knowledge. Nasafi replies by distinguishing acts: involuntary movements (like trembling) are divine acts, while voluntary movements are human acts; yet they appear similar, so similarity cannot be based solely on the act being brought into existence. He then addresses the attribute of knowledge: God's knowledge is eternal (azalī), while human knowledge is temporal (muḥdath), so there is no genuine similarity between them. He ends by referencing the Najjāriyya sect's view that similarity is inherent in things themselves, not from an external factor.

Key Terms
فعل الله
فعل العبد
العلم الأزلي
العلم المحدث
النجارية
المرتعش
الاختياري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God and humans are both 'knowing', they are similar in that attribute.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that the nature of knowledge differs: God's knowledge is eternal (azalī), while human knowledge is temporal (muḥdath). This fundamental difference prevents real similarity.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Nasafi shows that similarity in the category of 'bringing into existence' does not imply similarity in the nature of attributes; divine knowledge is eternal, human knowledge is temporal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If even the acts of the tremulous are attributed to Allah, do you see the sheer magnitude of His action in every detail? How does this reshape your view of your own voluntary actions? Do you still take credit for your successes as if you are independent, or will you now thank Allah for every movement? Repent from any sense of self-sufficiency.
?
The Najjāriyya claimed similarity by essence. But you, in your daily life, do you ever subtly compare Allah's attributes to human qualities? Are you truly convinced that His knowledge is not like yours, or do you treat His knowledge as merely a bigger version of your own? Pause now and ask Allah to purify your heart from any likeness you have imagined.

Similarity Between Opposites: A Kalam Dilemma
Nasafi presents an objection about similarity between opposites and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the kalam dialectical objection about similarity between opposites and Nasafi's refutation, clarifying that accidental similarity does not entail essential similarity.

Core Idea
Similarity in action does not imply similarity in essence.

Nasafi tackles a subtle objection: if divine and human actions can be similar (e.g., both being 'obedience'), then opposites like creation and command would also be similar. He refutes this by distinguishing between essential difference and accidental agreement. Let's examine the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'If he says: Yes...' and 'If he says: No...'. This is a classic kalam dilemma.
The objector presents two horns of a dilemma.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
The first horn: affirming similarity leads to absurdity (similarity between opposites). The second horn: denying similarity nullifies the agreement that obedience causes similarity despite essential difference.
Each horn is designed to force an unacceptable conclusion.
3
Understand Nasafi's refutation
Nasafi refutes by clarifying that similarity or difference in terms of obedience does not affect the essence itself. The objector's argument conflates accidental attributes with essential ones.
The refutation hinges on the distinction between essence (ذات) and attributes (صفات).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال : نعم، أوجب الاشتباه بين المتضادين مع اقتضاء ذاتيهما الاختلاف بينهما والذات المقتضى لذلك موجود
وإن قال : لا ، أبطل الاتفاق من حيث الطاعة أن يكون موجبا للتشابه عند الاختلاف في الذات، وكذا اختلافهما من حيث الطاعة لا يوجب الاختلاف بينهما عند استواء الذاتين و اقتضائهما تشابهها، والله والموفق.
If he says: Yes, it necessitates similarity between opposites despite their essences requiring difference and the essence requiring that exists. And if he says: No, he nullifies the agreement that obedience is a cause of similarity when there is difference in essence, and likewise their difference in terms of obedience does not necessitate difference between them when the essences are equal and require similarity. And God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer structure typical of kalam dialectic. The objector posits a dilemma: if one affirms similarity between divine and human actions, it implies similarity between opposites (since divine actions include creation and command which are opposite in essence), which is absurd. If one denies similarity, then the agreement that actions can be similar in being obedient is nullified when there is a difference in essence. The author refutes by clarifying that similarity or difference in terms of obedience does not affect the essence itself. The conclusion is that God is the ultimate guide.

Key Terms
اشتباه
متضادان
ذات
طاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that similarity in accidents (like being obedient) implies similarity in essence.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that accidental similarity does not necessitate essential similarity; essences remain distinct.

Checkpoint
What does the objector claim if one says that divine and human acts can be similar?
A) It necessitates similarity between opposites
B) It proves divine transcendence
C) It nullifies the concept of obedience
D) It establishes a middle ground

Key Takeaway
Similarity in attributes like obedience does not necessitate similarity in essence or the opposite status of actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Are there areas in your life where you judge your own worth by external actions rather than your essence before Allah? What would change if you focused on your inner state instead?
?
If similarity in obedience does not imply similarity in essence, then your acts of worship do not define your spiritual rank. How does that truth either relieve or unsettle you, and what will you do with that freedom?

Defending Divine Transcendence Against Objections of Evil and Knowledge Similarity
Nasafi responds to two objections about evil creations and knowledge similarity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi defends the absolute transcendence of God's creation and knowledge against objections based on the presence of evil in creation and the apparent similarity between divine and human knowledge.

Core Idea
God's knowledge is eternal; human knowledge is temporal — no real similarity.

The opponent raises two objections against the claim that God's creation is absolutely transcendent. First, if God creates lowly and evil things, then His creation seems similar to ours. Second, if both are 'bringing into existence,' then God as Knower would be similar to us as knowers. Nasafi answers both by pointing to the already established distinction in actions and the radical difference in the modality of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection about lowly creations
Pay attention to how the opponent uses the presence of evil and imperfection in creation to argue that divine and human creation cannot be truly distinct.
The opponent lists specific examples like devil, stench, filth.
2
Read the second objection about knowledge similarity
Notice how the opponent extends the argument from actions to attributes: if both acts are 'bringing into existence,' then God as Knower would be similar to us as knowers.
3
Read Nasafi's answer carefully
First, Nasafi dismisses the second objection as corrupt. Then he references the earlier discussion about movements to handle the action similarity. Finally, he specifies that God's knowledge is eternal while human knowledge is temporal, breaking any similarity.
The answer distinguishes between similarity in action (which is acceptable) and similarity in essence (which is denied for knowledge).
4
Reflect on the argument's structure
Consider why the modality of knowledge (eternal vs. temporal) is sufficient to negate similarity between God and creatures, even if the acts are similar in being acts of bringing into existence.
This protects divine transcendence without denying that God creates all things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن عندهم قد يكون فعل الله تعالى ما هو ذلك وخضوع لأن خلق الله مع تعالى عندهم المخلوق، ولا شك أن كل مخلوق فيه ذلة وخضوع وحاجة، ومن المخلوقات ما هو شيطان وشر وفتنة وابتلاء وفساد ونتن وخبث وقذرة، وكل ذلك عندهم فعل الله تعالى، فأنى يصح ما ذكر من الفرق وإبطال التشابه بين خلق الله تعالى وبين خلق غيره؟!
فإن قالوا: لو كان يقع الاشتباه بين فعلنا وفعل الله تعالى لأن كل واحد من الفعلين إخراج من العدم إلى الوجود وإحداث لكان الاشتباه بين الله وبين الخلق ثابتا لأنه تعالى عالم والعبد أيضا عالم.
قيل له: هذا الكلام فاسد، فإن الكلام قد سبق أن حركة المرتعش وحركات العروق النابضة فعل الله تعالى عندهم والحركة الاختيارية فعل العبد، وبينهما متشابهه ولا يمكن إثبات مخالفة بينهما في ذاتيهما على ما قررنا.
فأما الله تعالى فهو عالم بعلم أزلي والعبد عالم بعلم محدث، فلا يكون بين العالمين مشابهة.
That according to them, the act of God Almighty may be something of that and humility because the creation of God with Him is the creature, and there is no doubt that every creature has lowliness and humility and need, and among the creatures are the devil, evil, temptation, trial, corruption, stench, filth, and impurity, and all of that according to them is the act of God Almighty. So how can the mentioned distinction and the nullification of similarity between the creation of God Almighty and the creation of others be valid? Then they said: If similarity were to occur between our act and the act of God Almighty because each of the two acts is a bringing out from non-existence to existence and a bringing into being, then similarity between God and the creature would be established because He is knower and the servant is also knower. It was said to him: This speech is corrupt, for the speech has already preceded that the movement of the tremulous and the movements of the pulsating veins are the act of God Almighty according to them, and the voluntary movement is the act of the servant, and between them is similarity, and it is not possible to establish opposition between them in their essences as we have established. As for God Almighty, He is knower with eternal knowledge, and the servant is knower with temporal knowledge, so there is no similarity between the two knowers.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage contains two objections and a single answer. First, the opponent argues that if God creates evil and lowly things (like the devil, filth), then there is no real distinction between divine and human creation, and the claim of dissimilarity fails. Second, the opponent argues that if actions are similar in being brought into existence, then God and creatures would be similar in being knowers. Nasafi responds by pointing out that previous discussion already established that movements of tremors and veins are God's acts, while voluntary movement is the servant's act, and they are similar in essence (both are movements). However, regarding knowledge, God's knowledge is eternal while the servant's is temporal, so no similarity holds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that similarity in the category of action implies similarity in the essence of the agent.
Correction: Nasafi shows that similarity in action (e.g., both are bringing into existence) does not entail similarity in the knower, because the modality of knowledge (eternal vs. temporal) is fundamentally different.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi argue that there is no similarity between God's knowledge and human knowledge?
A) Because God's knowledge is not an attribute
B) Because God's knowledge is eternal while human knowledge is temporal
C) Because human knowledge is not real knowledge
D) Because knowledge is not an attribute of God

Key Takeaway
Nasafi defends divine transcendence by showing that the similarity in the act of creation does not entail similarity in the knower, because God's knowledge is eternal while human knowledge is temporal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You read that God creates even evil, temptation, and filth. When you face trials or injustices, do you truly believe that those too are from God? How does that belief sit with your natural tendency to blame others or yourself? What would change in your heart if you consistently saw every difficulty as God's act, just as you see blessings?
?
Nasafi insists that God's knowledge is eternal while yours is temporal. In what specific area of your life are you most tempted to assume that your limited, time-bound understanding of a situation is how God sees it? What would it mean for you to surrender that assumption and trust His eternal knowledge instead?
?
If similarity between divine and human action does not imply similarity in essence, then you cannot judge God's actions by human standards. Think of a time you were angry at God for something that felt unjust. Could you now re-evaluate that event not as a human-like mistake, but as an act of a being whose knowledge and wisdom are altogether different from yours? Will you actively remind yourself of this difference the next time your heart questions His decree?

Refuting al-Ka'bi's Objection and Distinguishing Islamic Schools
Nasafi distinguishes the responses of Ash'aris and Najjariyya to al-Ka'bi's objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi responds to al-Ka'bi's objection by showing that the Ash'aris and Najjariyya/Ahl al-Hadith are not subject to the charge of resemblance.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila objection misfires on different schools because they deny human agency differently.

This lesson presents the first part of Imam Nasafi's refutation of al-Ka'bi's argument. Al-Ka'bi claimed that those who say human acts are like God's acts are more liable to resemblance if they claim identity. Nasafi shows that the Ash'aris (who deny human agency) and the Najjariyya/Ahl al-Hadith (who affirm agency by acquisition) escape the objection.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ka'bi's objection
Begin by reading the opening lines where al-Ka'bi presents his claim. Note that he accuses the Maturidis of being more liable to the charge of resemblance.
The objection is from al-Ka'bi's Maqalat.
2
Identify the Ash'ari response
Nasafi explains that the Ash'aris and Abu Isa al-Warraq identify act with object, thus they deny the servant is an agent. The objection does not apply to them.
3
Identify the Najjariyya/Ahl al-Hadith response
These groups say the servant acts by acquisition (kasb) of what God originates, not by origination. So their act is not creation.
Acquisition (kasb) is a key term.
4
Recognize the rebounding of the objection
Nasafi concludes that the objection actually applies to the Mu'tazila themselves, who claim to create like God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا اعتراض الكعبي ذكر في المقالات فإن قالوا إنا إن قلنا: إنا نفعل مثل فعل ربنا، ولكن لا شك أن فعلنا غير فعل ربنا وإنكم تزعمون أنكم تفعلون عين فعل ربكم فأنتم أحق بالقول باشتباه فعلكم بفعل ربكم. قلنا لهم : أما الأشعرية وأبو عيسى البرغوث من النجارية فإنهم إن زعموا أن الفعل عين المفعول فإنهم يأبون أن يكون العبد فاعلاً فلا يستقيم قولكم في حقهم إنكم تفعلون فعل ربكم، فسقط كلامكم في حقهم. ومن قال من النجارية ومتكلمي أهل الحديث : أن العبد يفعل إلا أن فعله الاكتساب لما أحدثه الله تعالى لا الإحداث فهؤلاء وإن قرروا بالفعل ولكن فعلهم ليس بخلق فلم يكونوا خلقوا كخلق الله تعالى وأنتم الخالقون بزعمكم كخلق الله تعالى؛ فلزمكم هذا الكلام وسقط عنهم. وعندنا فعل العبد هوا مخلوق الله تعالى ومفعوله لا فعله وخلقه إذ فعل الله تعالى هو الصفة الأزلية القائمة بذاته، وما هو فعل العبد فهو مفعول الله تعالى، والله تعالى هو الذي تولى إيجاده وإخراجه من العدم إلى الوجود، والعبد اكتسبه وباشره فلم يكن فعل العبد مثل فعله ولا خلقه كخلقه، وكيف يكون كذلك ولا خلق للعبد البتة. ومما يكشف عن عوار هذا الكلام أن الاشتباه يجري بين شيئين، وعندكم فعلكم غير فعل الله تعالى فكانت إحدى الحركتين عندكم فعل العبد والأخرى فعل الله تعالى وهما متشابهتان، فوجد منكم على زعمكم خلق كخلق الله تعالى، فأما عندنا من يسلم لكم من النجارية ومتكلمي أهل الحديث أن العبد له فعل ففعله عندهم عين فعل الله تعالى، فهو من حيث إنه خلق فعل الله تعالى ومن حيث إنه حركة أو سكون طاعة أو معصية فعل العبد، فعين الكسب هو عين الخلق، وعين الخلق هو عين الكسب، كما أن عين الحركة هو عين الشيء وعين الشيء هو عين الحركة وإثبات الاشتباه في شيء واحد محال إذ الشيء لا يشبه نفسه، فكان إلزامكم إياهم فاسد. فعل الله خلق وإيجاد وفعل العبد مباشرة واكتساب فلم يلزم التشابه، والله الموفق.
This is the objection of al-Ka'bi mentioned in his Maqalat. They said: 'If we say we do the like of the act of our Lord, but there is no doubt that our act is other than the act of our Lord, and you claim that you do the very act of your Lord, then you are more entitled to say that your act resembles the act of your Lord.' We said to them: 'As for the Ash'aris and Abu Isa al-Warraq of the Najjariyya, they, if they claim that the act is the same as the object of the act, they refuse that the servant be an agent, so your saying—that you do the act of your Lord—is not valid concerning them; thus your argument falls regarding them. And among the Najjariyya and the speculative theologians of the Ahl al-Hadith, those who say that the servant does act, except that his act is acquisition (al-iktisab) of what God has originated, not origination (al-ihdath); these, though they are affirmed as acting, yet their act is not creation (khalq), so they have not created like the creation of God. And you are, according to your claim, creators like the creation of God; so this argument is necessary against you and falls away from them. According to us, the act of the servant is created by God and is His object (maf'ul), not His act (fi'l) nor His creation (khalq), because the act of God is the eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, and what is the act of the servant is the object of God. God is the one who undertakes its bringing into existence and bringing it out from non-existence into existence, while the servant acquires it and directly performs it. So the act of the servant is not like His act, nor is his creation like His creation. How could it be so, when there is no creation for the servant at all? And what exposes the fault of this speech is that resemblance occurs between two things. According to you, your act is other than the act of God. So, according to you, one of the two motions is the act of the servant and the other is the act of God, and they are similar. Thus, according to your claim, there occurred from you creation like the creation of God. But according to us, those of the Najjariyya and the speculative theologians of the Ahl al-Hadith who concede to you that the servant has an act, their view is that his act is the very act of God. So it is, from the aspect that it is creation (khalq), the act of God, and from the aspect that it is motion or stillness, obedience or disobedience, it is the act of the servant. So the very acquisition (kasb) is the very creation (khalq), and the very creation is the very acquisition, just as the very motion is the very thing and the very thing is the very motion. Affirming resemblance in a single thing is impossible, for a thing does not resemble itself. Hence your objection against them is invalid. God's act is creation and bringing into existence; our act is direct performance and acquisition. So resemblance does not necessarily occur. And God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection from the Mu'tazila theologian al-Ka'bi, followed by an exposition of the Maturidi doctrine of acquisition (kasb). The argument proceeds as follows: First, al-Ka'bi's objection is presented: the Mu'tazila claim that if the Maturidis say they do an act like God's, yet their act is different from God's, the Maturidis are more liable to the charge of resemblance because they claim their act is identical to God's. In response, Imam Nasafi distinguishes between different groups: The Ash'aris and Abu Isa al-Warraq, who identify act with the object, deny that the servant acts, so the objection does not apply to them. The Najjariyya and the speculative theologians of Ahl al-Hadith hold that the servant acts by acquisition (iktisab) of what God originates, not by origination itself, so their act is not creation. Hence the Mu'tazila, who claim humans create like God, incur the objection, not these groups. Then the Maturidi position is stated: the act of the servant is created by God (makhluq) and is His object (maf'ul), not His act (fi'l) nor creation (khalq), because God's act is His eternal attribute. God brings the act into existence, and the servant acquires it and directly performs it. Therefore, there is no similarity between divine and human action. The passage then clarifies a further point: similarity requires two distinct things. In the Mu'tazila view, their act is other than God's act, so there are two distinct motions that are similar, thus they do produce creation like God's. But according to the Najjariyya and Ahl al-Hadith, the act of the servant is exactly the act of God in terms of creation, but it is also the servant's act in terms of motion/obedience. Thus the acquisition and creation are identical, so resemblance in one thing is impossible. Finally, the conclusion is reinforced: God's act is creation and bringing into existence; our act is direct performance and acquisition, so no resemblance follows.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila think all Muslims who affirm human action (like Maturidis) are claiming identity with divine action.
Correction: This passage shows that different schools have different understandings of human action, and the Maturidi position is distinct.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group denies that the servant is an agent?
A) Ash'aris
B) Najjariyya
C) Ahl al-Hadith
D) Mu'tazila

Key Takeaway
Imam Nasafi shows that al-Ka'bi's objection does not apply to Ash'aris (who deny human agency) or to Najjariyya/Ahl al-Hadith (who see human act as acquisition, not creation).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that affirming human action does not make you a creator like Allah. But in your daily life, when you succeed at something, do you feel a sense of ownership that borders on attributing independent power to yourself? What would it take to shift that feeling into pure gratitude and reliance on the Creator?
?
The Mu'tazila thought they were defending divine justice by affirming human creation, but they fell into shirk in actions. Where have you justified a wrong action by over-emphasizing your own free will while forgetting that even your ability to choose is given by Allah? How will you repent for that misplaced independence?
?
You now know that Najjariyya and Ahl al-Hadith hold a balanced view: you act, but Allah creates. Is there an area of your life where you are either denying responsibility (thus slipping into Ash'ari-like fatalism) or claiming too much power (thus slipping into Mu'tazila-like arrogance)? Which one is your greater temptation, and what concrete step will you take today to correct it?

The Maturidi Doctrine of Acquisition (Kasb)
Nasafi states the Maturidi doctrine of kasb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi distinction between divine creation and human acquisition in action.

Core Idea
The servant's act is created by God but acquired by the servant.

This lesson presents the core Maturidi teaching on human action. Imam Nasafi states clearly that the act of the servant is created by God and is His object (maf'ul), not His act (fi'l) nor His creation (khalq). God is the sole creator, while the servant acquires the act and directly performs it.

Guided Path
1
Read the Maturidi position
Carefully read the passage defining the Maturidi view. Highlight the key terms: maf'ul, fi'l, khalq, kasb.
2
Identify the relationship
Understand that God creates the act and the servant acquires it. Note that God's act is His eternal attribute.
3
Note the distinction
The servant's act is not like God's act because the servant does not create. There is no creation for the servant at all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا اعتراض الكعبي ذكر في المقالات فإن قالوا إنا إن قلنا: إنا نفعل مثل فعل ربنا، ولكن لا شك أن فعلنا غير فعل ربنا وإنكم تزعمون أنكم تفعلون عين فعل ربكم فأنتم أحق بالقول باشتباه فعلكم بفعل ربكم. قلنا لهم : أما الأشعرية وأبو عيسى البرغوث من النجارية فإنهم إن زعموا أن الفعل عين المفعول فإنهم يأبون أن يكون العبد فاعلاً فلا يستقيم قولكم في حقهم إنكم تفعلون فعل ربكم، فسقط كلامكم في حقهم. ومن قال من النجارية ومتكلمي أهل الحديث : أن العبد يفعل إلا أن فعله الاكتساب لما أحدثه الله تعالى لا الإحداث فهؤلاء وإن قرروا بالفعل ولكن فعلهم ليس بخلق فلم يكونوا خلقوا كخلق الله تعالى وأنتم الخالقون بزعمكم كخلق الله تعالى؛ فلزمكم هذا الكلام وسقط عنهم. وعندنا فعل العبد هوا مخلوق الله تعالى ومفعوله لا فعله وخلقه إذ فعل الله تعالى هو الصفة الأزلية القائمة بذاته، وما هو فعل العبد فهو مفعول الله تعالى، والله تعالى هو الذي تولى إيجاده وإخراجه من العدم إلى الوجود، والعبد اكتسبه وباشره فلم يكن فعل العبد مثل فعله ولا خلقه كخلقه، وكيف يكون كذلك ولا خلق للعبد البتة. ومما يكشف عن عوار هذا الكلام أن الاشتباه يجري بين شيئين، وعندكم فعلكم غير فعل الله تعالى فكانت إحدى الحركتين عندكم فعل العبد والأخرى فعل الله تعالى وهما متشابهتان، فوجد منكم على زعمكم خلق كخلق الله تعالى، فأما عندنا من يسلم لكم من النجارية ومتكلمي أهل الحديث أن العبد له فعل ففعله عندهم عين فعل الله تعالى، فهو من حيث إنه خلق فعل الله تعالى ومن حيث إنه حركة أو سكون طاعة أو معصية فعل العبد، فعين الكسب هو عين الخلق، وعين الخلق هو عين الكسب، كما أن عين الحركة هو عين الشيء وعين الشيء هو عين الحركة وإثبات الاشتباه في شيء واحد محال إذ الشيء لا يشبه نفسه، فكان إلزامكم إياهم فاسد. فعل الله خلق وإيجاد وفعل العبد مباشرة واكتساب فلم يلزم التشابه، والله الموفق.
This is the objection of al-Ka'bi mentioned in his Maqalat. They said: 'If we say we do the like of the act of our Lord, but there is no doubt that our act is other than the act of our Lord, and you claim that you do the very act of your Lord, then you are more entitled to say that your act resembles the act of your Lord.' We said to them: 'As for the Ash'aris and Abu Isa al-Warraq of the Najjariyya, they, if they claim that the act is the same as the object of the act, they refuse that the servant be an agent, so your saying—that you do the act of your Lord—is not valid concerning them; thus your argument falls regarding them. And among the Najjariyya and the speculative theologians of the Ahl al-Hadith, those who say that the servant does act, except that his act is acquisition (al-iktisab) of what God has originated, not origination (al-ihdath); these, though they are affirmed as acting, yet their act is not creation (khalq), so they have not created like the creation of God. And you are, according to your claim, creators like the creation of God; so this argument is necessary against you and falls away from them. According to us, the act of the servant is created by God and is His object (maf'ul), not His act (fi'l) nor His creation (khalq), because the act of God is the eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, and what is the act of the servant is the object of God. God is the one who undertakes its bringing into existence and bringing it out from non-existence into existence, while the servant acquires it and directly performs it. So the act of the servant is not like His act, nor is his creation like His creation. How could it be so, when there is no creation for the servant at all? And what exposes the fault of this speech is that resemblance occurs between two things. According to you, your act is other than the act of God. So, according to you, one of the two motions is the act of the servant and the other is the act of God, and they are similar. Thus, according to your claim, there occurred from you creation like the creation of God. But according to us, those of the Najjariyya and the speculative theologians of the Ahl al-Hadith who concede to you that the servant has an act, their view is that his act is the very act of God. So it is, from the aspect that it is creation (khalq), the act of God, and from the aspect that it is motion or stillness, obedience or disobedience, it is the act of the servant. So the very acquisition (kasb) is the very creation (khalq), and the very creation is the very acquisition, just as the very motion is the very thing and the very thing is the very motion. Affirming resemblance in a single thing is impossible, for a thing does not resemble itself. Hence your objection against them is invalid. God's act is creation and bringing into existence; our act is direct performance and acquisition. So resemblance does not necessarily occur. And God is the giver of success.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Maturidi doctrine means humans create their own acts.
Correction: This passage clarifies that creation is exclusively God's, and human role is acquisition and direct performance.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi position, what is the role of the servant in his own act?
A) He creates it
B) He acquires it and performs it
C) He merely observes it
D) He has no role

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi view maintains a clear distinction: God creates the act, the servant acquires it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you tend to use the belief that 'God created it' as an excuse to avoid repentance, or do you fully own the act as your acquisition? How does this lesson convict you to hold both truths together?
?
If every good deed you do is ultimately created by God, where does that leave your pride? Will you thank Him for creating the act even as you rejoice in performing it?
?
How does knowing that you do not create your own actions — not even your most private thoughts — affect your view of your own independence? Is there an area of your life where you still act as if you are the ultimate creator?

Resemblance Requires Two Distinct Things - Final Refutation
Nasafi uses a logical argument about resemblance to refute the objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical refutation of the Mu'tazila objection based on the principle that resemblance requires two distinct things.

Core Idea
A thing cannot resemble itself; resemblance requires two distinct entities.

This lesson completes the refutation by exposing a logical flaw in the Mu'tazila objection. Al-Ka'bi's argument assumed that human and divine acts are both distinct and similar, but Nasafi shows that according to the Maturidi position (and even the Najjariyya/Ahl al-Hadith view), the act is one reality with two aspects, so self-resemblance is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle
Resemblance (tashabuh) requires two distinct things. A thing cannot resemble itself.
2
Examine the Mu'tazila view
In their view, human act and divine act are two distinct motions, so they are similar. This implies they create like God.
3
Examine the Najjariyya/Ahl al-Hadith view
They see the act as one reality: creation aspect is God's, motion aspect is servant's. So there is only one thing.
Acquisition and creation are identical.
4
Conclude the refutation
Since the act is one, resemblance is impossible, so the objection is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا اعتراض الكعبي ذكر في المقالات فإن قالوا إنا إن قلنا: إنا نفعل مثل فعل ربنا، ولكن لا شك أن فعلنا غير فعل ربنا وإنكم تزعمون أنكم تفعلون عين فعل ربكم فأنتم أحق بالقول باشتباه فعلكم بفعل ربكم. قلنا لهم : أما الأشعرية وأبو عيسى البرغوث من النجارية فإنهم إن زعموا أن الفعل عين المفعول فإنهم يأبون أن يكون العبد فاعلاً فلا يستقيم قولكم في حقهم إنكم تفعلون فعل ربكم، فسقط كلامكم في حقهم. ومن قال من النجارية ومتكلمي أهل الحديث : أن العبد يفعل إلا أن فعله الاكتساب لما أحدثه الله تعالى لا الإحداث فهؤلاء وإن قرروا بالفعل ولكن فعلهم ليس بخلق فلم يكونوا خلقوا كخلق الله تعالى وأنتم الخالقون بزعمكم كخلق الله تعالى؛ فلزمكم هذا الكلام وسقط عنهم. وعندنا فعل العبد هوا مخلوق الله تعالى ومفعوله لا فعله وخلقه إذ فعل الله تعالى هو الصفة الأزلية القائمة بذاته، وما هو فعل العبد فهو مفعول الله تعالى، والله تعالى هو الذي تولى إيجاده وإخراجه من العدم إلى الوجود، والعبد اكتسبه وباشره فلم يكن فعل العبد مثل فعله ولا خلقه كخلقه، وكيف يكون كذلك ولا خلق للعبد البتة. ومما يكشف عن عوار هذا الكلام أن الاشتباه يجري بين شيئين، وعندكم فعلكم غير فعل الله تعالى فكانت إحدى الحركتين عندكم فعل العبد والأخرى فعل الله تعالى وهما متشابهتان، فوجد منكم على زعمكم خلق كخلق الله تعالى، فأما عندنا من يسلم لكم من النجارية ومتكلمي أهل الحديث أن العبد له فعل ففعله عندهم عين فعل الله تعالى، فهو من حيث إنه خلق فعل الله تعالى ومن حيث إنه حركة أو سكون طاعة أو معصية فعل العبد، فعين الكسب هو عين الخلق، وعين الخلق هو عين الكسب، كما أن عين الحركة هو عين الشيء وعين الشيء هو عين الحركة وإثبات الاشتباه في شيء واحد محال إذ الشيء لا يشبه نفسه، فكان إلزامكم إياهم فاسد. فعل الله خلق وإيجاد وفعل العبد مباشرة واكتساب فلم يلزم التشابه، والله الموفق.
This is the objection of al-Ka'bi mentioned in his Maqalat. They said: 'If we say we do the like of the act of our Lord, but there is no doubt that our act is other than the act of our Lord, and you claim that you do the very act of your Lord, then you are more entitled to say that your act resembles the act of your Lord.' We said to them: 'As for the Ash'aris and Abu Isa al-Warraq of the Najjariyya, they, if they claim that the act is the same as the object of the act, they refuse that the servant be an agent, so your saying—that you do the act of your Lord—is not valid concerning them; thus your argument falls regarding them. And among the Najjariyya and the speculative theologians of the Ahl al-Hadith, those who say that the servant does act, except that his act is acquisition (al-iktisab) of what God has originated, not origination (al-ihdath); these, though they are affirmed as acting, yet their act is not creation (khalq), so they have not created like the creation of God. And you are, according to your claim, creators like the creation of God; so this argument is necessary against you and falls away from them. According to us, the act of the servant is created by God and is His object (maf'ul), not His act (fi'l) nor His creation (khalq), because the act of God is the eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, and what is the act of the servant is the object of God. God is the one who undertakes its bringing into existence and bringing it out from non-existence into existence, while the servant acquires it and directly performs it. So the act of the servant is not like His act, nor is his creation like His creation. How could it be so, when there is no creation for the servant at all? And what exposes the fault of this speech is that resemblance occurs between two things. According to you, your act is other than the act of God. So, according to you, one of the two motions is the act of the servant and the other is the act of God, and they are similar. Thus, according to your claim, there occurred from you creation like the creation of God. But according to us, those of the Najjariyya and the speculative theologians of the Ahl al-Hadith who concede to you that the servant has an act, their view is that his act is the very act of God. So it is, from the aspect that it is creation (khalq), the act of God, and from the aspect that it is motion or stillness, obedience or disobedience, it is the act of the servant. So the very acquisition (kasb) is the very creation (khalq), and the very creation is the very acquisition, just as the very motion is the very thing and the very thing is the very motion. Affirming resemblance in a single thing is impossible, for a thing does not resemble itself. Hence your objection against them is invalid. God's act is creation and bringing into existence; our act is direct performance and acquisition. So resemblance does not necessarily occur. And God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection from the Mu'tazila theologian al-Ka'bi, followed by an exposition of the Maturidi doctrine of acquisition (kasb). The argument proceeds as follows: First, al-Ka'bi's objection is presented: the Mu'tazila claim that if the Maturidis say they do an act like God's, yet their act is different from God's, the Maturidis are more liable to the charge of resemblance because they claim their act is identical to God's. In response, Imam Nasafi distinguishes between different groups: The Ash'aris and Abu Isa al-Warraq, who identify act with the object, deny that the servant acts, so the objection does not apply to them. The Najjariyya and the speculative theologians of Ahl al-Hadith hold that the servant acts by acquisition (iktisab) of what God originates, not by origination itself, so their act is not creation. Hence the Mu'tazila, who claim humans create like God, incur the objection, not these groups. Then the Maturidi position is stated: the act of the servant is created by God (makhluq) and is His object (maf'ul), not His act (fi'l) nor creation (khalq), because God's act is His eternal attribute. God brings the act into existence, and the servant acquires it and directly performs it. Therefore, there is no similarity between divine and human action. The passage then clarifies a further point: similarity requires two distinct things. In the Mu'tazila view, their act is other than God's act, so there are two distinct motions that are similar, thus they do produce creation like God's. But according to the Najjariyya and Ahl al-Hadith, the act of the servant is exactly the act of God in terms of creation, but it is also the servant's act in terms of motion/obedience. Thus the acquisition and creation are identical, so resemblance in one thing is impossible. Finally, the conclusion is reinforced: God's act is creation and bringing into existence; our act is direct performance and acquisition, so no resemblance follows.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Maturidi doctrine makes human and divine acts identical in every way.
Correction: This passage clarifies that they are identical in terms of the created object but distinct in terms of agency.

Checkpoint

A) Because resemblance cannot occur in a single thing
B) Because the Mu'tazila are wrong about creation
C) Because the Ash'aris deny agency
D) Because the Qur'an says otherwise

Key Takeaway
Resemblance requires two distinct things; since the act is one reality with two aspects, the charge of resemblance is impossible.

Will you now see your obedience and disobedience as a direct encounter with the Creator? How does this change how you approach your next sin or act of worship?
?
The Mu'tazila insisted on a distinction to protect God's justice. But Nasafi says that distinction leads to resemblance and thus a form of shirk in a way. Have you ever argued for something that seemed logical but actually undermined tawhid? What will you do the next time you rely on human reason over revelation?
?
If everything you do—every motion, every stillness—is from God's creation, then your very existence is an act of God. Are you living as if you are an act of God? Or are you acting as if you are independent? What one thing will you change today to acknowledge that your entire being is from Him?

Refuting Similarity Between Divine and Human Acts
The author argues that essential similarity is unaffected by agent, refuting Mu'tazilite views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing creative power to anyone other than Allah leads to impossibility and disbelief, according to Maturidi reasoning.

Core Idea
Essential similarity between acts cannot be overridden by the agent's identity.

This passage presents a key logical principle in Maturidi kalam: two things that are alike in essence remain alike regardless of who does them. The author applies this to the Mu'tazilite claim that human acts are similar to God's creation, showing that this leads to a denial of the Quran and the possibility of worshipping created beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
2
Identify the logical principle
Find the author's central claim about similarity in essence and the irrelevance of agent, place, time, etc.
The principle is stated early in the passage.
3
Examine the examples given
Notice the examples of movements, blackness/whiteness, etc., to see how the principle works in practice.
4
Understand the application to Mu'tazila
See how the author applies this principle to refute the Mu'tazilite view, and how it leads to the Quranic argument.
The Quranic verse is cited to reinforce the point.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why the author says attributing creative power to others leads to impossibility. How does this connect to tawhid?
This step ties the lesson to broader theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول: قد سبق الكلام أن المشتبهين بذاتيهما لا يختلفان باختلاف الفاعلين ولا باختلاف معاني وراء ذاتيهما، ولا عبرة لاختلاف الفاعل واتحاده، إنما العبرة في معرفة حقيقة الاشتباه لذات المشتبهين أو المعنى الموجب للاشتباه لا لما وراء ذلك من الفاعل أو المكان أو الزمان أو الآلة أو السبب، لأن كل ذلك لا يوجب التغير في علة الاشتباه أو الاختلاف، ولهذا لم يكن بين الحركتين من جهتين مختلفتين وبين الحركة والسكون وبين السواد والبياض والاجتماع والافتراق والحلاوة والمرارة والنتن والرائحة الطيبة مشابهة عند اتحاد الفاعل، فكذا لا يوجب اختلاف الفاعلين اختلافا في الفعلين عند اشتباههما بذاتيهما. وتحقق ما رمنا تحقيقه من إثبات المشابهة بين خلق الله تعالى وخلق العباد على أصول المعتزلة، والله تعالى نفى ذلك فصاروا بذلك رادين على الله تعالى وجاعلين أنفسهم مستحقة للعبادة وأهلاً لها لأن الله تعالى بقوله: ﴿ أم جعلوا لله شركاء خلقوا كخلقه فتشابه الخلق عليهم ﴾ أوجب لهم العذر في عبادتهم ما كانوا يعبدون وجعلهم إياهم شركاء الله تعالى في العبادة لو كان منهم خلق كخلقه، وكل ذلك كفر عصمنا الله تعالى عن مثل ذلك. وبالوقوف على ما بينا ظهرت صحة ما ادعينا أن إثبات قدرة التخليق لغير الله تعالى يؤدي إلى المحال، وبالله التوفيق.
Then we say: It has already been stated that two things that are similar in their essences do not differ due to difference of agents nor due to difference of meanings beyond their essences, and there is no consideration for the difference or unity of the agent; consideration is only in knowing the reality of the similarity in the essence of the two similar things or the meaning that necessitates similarity, not for what is beyond that of the agent, place, time, instrument, or cause, because all of that does not necessitate change in the cause of similarity or difference. For this reason, there is no similarity between two movements from two different directions, between movement and rest, between blackness and whiteness, conjunction and separation, sweetness and bitterness, foul smell and pleasant smell, when the agent is one; so likewise, difference of agents does not necessitate difference in the two actions when they are similar in their essences. And what we intended to establish, of proving similarity between the creation of Allah Most High and the creation of servants according to the principles of the Mu'tazila, is realized; but Allah Most High denied that, so they thereby become rejecters of Allah and consider themselves deserving of worship and fit for it, because Allah Most High by His saying: “Or have they assigned partners to Allah who create as He creates, so that the creation is similar to them?” obligated an excuse for them in worshipping what they used to worship and made them partners of Allah in worship if there were from them creation like His creation; and all of that is disbelief – Allah protect us from such. And by reflecting on what we have explained, the correctness of what we claimed appears: that attributing the power of creation to other than Allah Most High leads to impossibility. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite claim that there is similarity between God's creation and human acts. The author begins by stating a logical principle: two things that are alike in their essences (مشتبهان بذاتيهما) cannot differ due to external factors such as the agent, place, time, etc. The only relevant consideration is the essence itself or the meaning that causes the similarity. The author provides examples: two movements from different directions, or movement and rest, etc., show no similarity even when the agent is one. Similarly, difference of agents does not create difference between actions that are essentially alike. The author then applies this to the Mu'tazilite position: if they claim that God's creation and human creation are similar in essence, then they are rejecting God's denial of such similarity in the Quran (Surah Ar-Ra'd, 13:16). He argues that if human creation were truly like God's creation, then worshipping created beings would be excused, making them partners with God – which is clear disbelief. Therefore, attributing creative power (قدرة التخليق) to anyone other than God is absurd and impossible.

Key Terms
مشتبهان
ذات
فاعل
قدرة التخليق
إثبات المشابهة
معتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that similarity of actions implies similarity of agents.
Correction: The author clarifies that external factors like the agent do not affect essential similarity; two actions can be similar in essence regardless of who performs them.

Checkpoint

A) Because it contradicts the Quran which denies such similarity.
B) Because humans cannot create anything at all.
C) Because similarity would obligate worshipping human creators.
D) Both A and C.

Key Takeaway
Attributing the power of creation to anyone other than Allah leads to impossibility and kufr, because essential similarity between acts is independent of the agent and contradicts divine revelation.

The author says that if human acts were essentially like divine creation, then those acts would be worthy of worship. Is there any area of your life where you secretly admire your own 'creations'—your wealth, status, or relationships—as if they were independent of Allah? How can you use today's reading to recalibrate your heart's allegiance?
?

If there is hesitation, what is the root cause, and how will you uproot it before the day ends?

Refuting the Claim that Power Relates Only to Origination
Objection and refutation regarding the scope of power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi refutes the claim that divine power is limited to origination, and how he directs the opponent to engage with the established proof.

Core Idea
Power is not confined to origination; the burden of proof is on the opponent.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi addresses a key objection raised by those who argue that power (qudra) only relates to bringing things into existence. He counters by pointing to an earlier proof that establishes the impossibility of anyone other than God having the power of invention and origination. Thus, the opponent must challenge the proof itself rather than simply assert their claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the opponents' claim that 'power has no relation except to origination, and its relation to the aspect of origination is not intelligible.' Notice that they assert both a positive claim and a negative implication.
2
Identify the author's response strategy
See how the author does not directly argue about the nature of power. Instead, he references an already established proof that the power of invention and origination is impossible for anyone other than God. This shifts the burden of proof onto the opponent.
The response is a classic argumentative move: redirect the opponent to a more fundamental proof.
3
Understand the burden-shifting technique
The opponent must now object to the proof itself, not simply restate their claim. This forces them to engage with the earlier evidence rather than making an assertion.
4
Reflect on the broader theological significance
Consider why limiting power to origination is problematic for Islamic theology. It would imply that God's power is confined, which contradicts His omnipotence. The proof against others having such power safeguards God's unique attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبهذا يجابون عن قولهم : إن لا تعلق للقدرة إلا بالإحداث وتعلقها بوجه الإحداث غير معقول. فإنا نقول لهم : قد أقمنا الدلالة على استحالة ثبوت قدرة الاختراع والإحداث لغير الله تعالى فعليكم أن تعترضوا على ذلك الدليل.
And with this they are answered concerning their statement: 'Power has no relation except to origination (ihdath), and its relation to the aspect of origination is not intelligible.' For we say to them: 'We have established the proof of the impossibility of the existence of the power of invention (ikhtira') and origination (ihdath) for other than God Almighty, so you must object to that proof.'
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The opponents claim that power (qudra) is only related to bringing something into existence (ihdath), and that relating it to any other aspect is unintelligible. The author responds by stating that the proof has already been established showing that the power of invention and origination is impossible for anyone other than God. Therefore, the opponents are directed to attack that proof itself rather than simply asserting the claim. The answer shifts the burden back to the opponent.

الاختراع

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's power is limited to bringing things into existence, and that the concept of power relating to other aspects is unintelligible.
Correction: The author shows that such a claim is not a self-evident truth but must be defended against the proof that excludes others from having such power. The opponent must engage with that proof.

Checkpoint
What is the opponents' claim in this passage?
A) Power has no relation except to origination.
B) Power can relate to anything.
C) The servant has no power at all.
D) God's power is limited.

Key Takeaway
Imam Nasafi refutes the opponent by asserting that the burden of proof lies on them to challenge the established proof against anyone other than God having the power of origination.

?

When you wake up tomorrow, will you consciously acknowledge that your very existence is being sustained by the same power that originated it? Or will you slip back into taking it for granted?
?
The author shifted the burden to the opponent by saying 'you must object to that proof.' When doubts creep into your heart about God's exclusive power to create and sustain, do you honestly seek to examine your own proofs, or do you remain satisfied with surface-level assumptions? The Knowledge-Power Analogy Objection
Objection comparing knowledge and power to demand identical enabling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that compares divine knowledge and power, claiming that enabling must grant the same aspect as God's power.

Core Idea
Power and knowledge are not analogous in their attachment to objects.

Before examining Imam al-Nasafi's refutation, we must first grasp the objection. The opponents draw a parallel between how God informs us and how He enables us, arguing that just as information must match reality, enabling must grant the same aspect of power. This lesson presents that objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: it begins with a heading, then presents the analogy from knowledge, then applies it to power.
The phrase 'As mentioned earlier' refers to prior context.
2
Identify the key claim
The objectors claim that if God enables us, He must enable us in the same aspect (invention) as His own power. Find the sentence that states this.
3
Understand the analogy
The objection is based on an analogy from knowledge: just as informing must match reality, so enabling must match power. Reflex on why this analogy might be flawed.
This sets up the need for a distinction between knowledge and power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبهة والرد عليها
وهكذا الجواب عن قولهم إن الله تعالى إذا علم شيئا ثم أعلمنا إنما يكون ما يثبت علمه بذلك الشيء، أي لو أعلمنا على الوجه الذي علم هو به، فأما إذا أعلمنا لا على ذلك الوجه لا يكون ذلك إعلاماً بل يكون ذلك تجهيلاً، فإنه تعالى إذا علم شيئًا أسود أو أبيض أو طويلاً أو عريضا فإن أعلمنا على ذلك الوجه بأن أعلمنا أنه أسود أو أبيض وعلى ما كان كان ما ثبت لنا علمًا وإن علم هو شيئًا أسود وأعلمنا أبيض فما ثبت لنا لا يكون علمًا بل يكون جهلاً، فكذا هذا في قدرته وإقداره إيانا، فإذا قدر على شيء وأقدرنا عليه ينبغي أن يقدرنا على ذلك الوجه ولو أقدرنا لا على ذلك الوجه لا يكون ذلك إقدار ثم إنه تعالى يقدر اختراع الأشياء فإذا أقدرنا يقدرنا على جهة الاختراع، ولو لم يقدرنا على تلك الجهة لا يكون ذلك إقدارا.
لما مر
فإنا نجيب عن هذا الكلام فنقول: بل يكون ذلك إقدارًا وإن لم يقدرنا على الاختراع أن للعبد فعلاً يتعلق به قدرته، وأن ثبوت الاختراع من جهته مستحيل، وثبت بمجموع الدليلين أن المقدور نوعان: مخترع ومكتسب، والقدرة تتعلق بالمقدور بجهتين جهة اختراع وجهة اكتساب اختص الله تعالى بأحدهما واختص المحدث بالآخر، بخلاف العلم فإن هناك لم يثبت دليل يوجب أن يعلق العلم بالمعلوم بجهتين بل قام الدليل أن تعلقه بالمعلوم بجهة واحدة وهو أن يتعلق به على ما هو به، إذ لو تعلق به لا على هذه الجهة لكان جهلاً لا علمًا.
ثم نشتغل بإبطال ذلك فنقول: قياس العلم يقتضي ما قلنا لو عقلتم، فإن علمنا يتعلق بما هو معلوم الله تعالى وليس من ضرورة تعلق علمنا به زوال علم الباري جل وعلا بل بقي علمه متعلقا به، وبقي المعلوم معلومًا له وإن صار معلومًا لنا، فكذا قدرتنا ينبغي أن تتعلق بما هو مقدور الله تعالى وعند تعلق قدرتنا به يبقى مقدورًا له، وكانت قدرته للاختراع فيبقى كذلك وكون الشيء مخترعًا بقدرتين.
An Objection and its Refutation. And likewise the answer to their statement that if Allah knows something and then informs us, only that would occur which verifies His knowledge of that thing, meaning if He informs us in the manner in which He knows it. But if He informs us not in that manner, that would not be informing but rather would be misleading. For if He knows a thing black or white or long or broad, and He informs us in that manner by informing us that it is black or white and as it is, what is established for us is knowledge. But if He knows a thing black and informs us white, what is established for us is not knowledge but ignorance. So likewise this regarding His power and His enabling us. So if He is able over something and enables us over it, it should be that He enables us in that manner; if He enables us not in that manner, that would not be enabling. Then He is able to invent things, so if He enables us, He enables us in the aspect of invention; if He did not enable us in that aspect, that would not be enabling. As mentioned earlier. So we answer this speech by saying: Rather, that is enabling even if He does not enable us to invent, because the servant has an act to which his power is attached, and that invention from his side is impossible, and it is established by the combination of the two proofs that the acquired power is of two types: invented and acquired. Power attaches to the acquired in two aspects: aspect of invention and aspect of acquisition. Allah is specialized with one of them and the originated being is specialized with the other, unlike knowledge, because there no proof has been established that obligates that knowledge be attached to the known in two aspects; rather the proof has established that its attachment to the known is in one aspect, which is to attach to it as it is, because if it attached to it not in that aspect, it would be ignorance, not knowledge. Then we proceed to invalidate that by saying: The analogy of knowledge would necessitate what we said, if you understand. For our knowledge attaches to what is known by Allah, and it is not necessary that by the attachment of our knowledge to it the knowledge of Allah be removed; rather His knowledge remains attached to it, and the known remains known to Him even if it becomes known to us. So likewise our power should attach to what is an object of power for Allah, and when our power attaches to it, it remains an object of power for Him. And His power is for invention, so it remains so, and the thing being invented by two powers.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a second objection-and-answer unit, beginning with a heading 'An Objection and its Refutation'. The objection draws an analogy from knowledge to power: if God knows something, He must inform us exactly as He knows it; otherwise it would be misleading. Similarly, if God has power over something and enables us, He must enable us in the same manner—i.e., with the aspect of invention. If He enables us only in a different manner (acquisition), that would not be true enabling. The response has two parts. First, the direct answer: enabling is valid even without invention, because we have proven that the servant has an act, and invention from the servant is impossible. The combination of proofs shows that the object of power (maqdūr) is of two types: invented (mukhtara') and acquired (muktasab). Power attaches in two aspects: invention (exclusive to God) and acquisition (exclusive to humans). Knowledge is different because no proof allows two aspects; knowledge must attach as the object actually is. Second, a further refutation: Actually, the analogy of knowledge supports our position. Our knowledge attaching to something known by God does not remove God's knowledge; similarly, our power attaching to something God is powerful over does not remove God's power. So the same thing can be an object of two powers—God's (invention) and human's (acquisition). Thus, the objection fails because it falsely assumes a parallel where none exists. The passage carefully distinguishes the epistemologies of knowledge and power, and defends the Maturidi doctrine of kasb.

Key Terms
قدرة
إقدار
علم
إعلام
اختراع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the objection, if God knows something black and informs us white, what is the result?
A) We gain knowledge
B) We gain ignorance
C) We gain partial knowledge
D) We gain certainty

Key Takeaway
The objection draws a strict analogy between knowledge and power, demanding that enabling must mirror God's power in aspect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider God's knowledge of every detail of your life—including your sins and failures—do you truly believe that He communicates to you only what is true and just? How does this confidence (or lack thereof) affect your daily walk with Him?
?
The objector demands that enabling grant the exact same capacity as God's power. In your own life, when you feel God has not given you the abilities you expected or desired, do you become resentful or accuse Him of being unjust? What would it take for you to trust that His enabling, though different, is still sufficient and wise?
?
Are there areas in your life where you secretly demand that God act toward you in exactly the way you imagine He should—based on your limited understanding—rather than submitting to His perfect wisdom? What would it look like to surrender that demand today?

The Direct Answer: Power Has Two Aspects
Direct refutation introducing the two-aspect theory of power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Nasafi's direct response that enabling is valid even without granting invention, because power attaches in two distinct aspects.

Core Idea
Power has two aspects: invention for God, acquisition for humans.

Having presented the objection, Imam al-Nasafi now delivers his answer. He introduces the key distinction: the object of power is either invented or acquired, and power attaches in two aspects—invention and acquisition. This lesson unpacks that response.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the shift: 'So we answer this speech by saying...'.
2
Identify the two types of maqdūr
Find where the author says the object of power is of two types: invented (mukhtara') and acquired (muktasab).
This is a key distinction.
3
Note the contrast with knowledge
Observe how the author distinguishes power from knowledge: knowledge attaches in only one aspect, but power attaches in two.
This directly refutes the analogy.

Source Text

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Divine enabling must grant the exact same kind of power (invention) as God's power.
Correction: Enabling is valid even without invention because power has two aspects; humans are enabled for acquisition only.

According to the answer, how many aspects does power attach to the maqdūr?
A) one
B) two
C) three
D) none

Key Takeaway
Power attaches in two distinct aspects—invention for God, acquisition for humans—so enabling does not require replicating divine invention.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you attribute your actions to yourself, do you truly see them as your acquisition or do you secretly think you invented them? How does this misattribution affect your humility before Allah?
?
If knowledge must attach to reality exactly as it is, where in your life have you been content to know things not as they are but as you wish them to be? Are you willing to abandon that distortion today?
?
You have power over some things (acquisition) and no power over others (invention). Which invented outcomes are you chasing as if you could create them? Will you stop and let Allah be the only Inventor?

The Further Refutation: Turning the Analogy Around
Further refutation showing that the analogy actually supports coexistence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Nasafi uses the analogy of knowledge to argue that two powers can coexist on the same object.

Core Idea
The analogy of knowledge proves that two powers can coexist on the same object.

After giving the direct answer, Imam al-Nasafi goes further. He argues that the analogy of knowledge, properly understood, supports his claim that our power can attach to what God is powerful over without removing God's power. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the further refutation
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the phrase 'Then we proceed to invalidate that by saying...'.
2
Understand the analogy from knowledge
The author points out that our knowledge attaches to what Allah knows without removing His knowledge. This is the premise.
This is a fact about knowledge.
3
Apply the analogy to power
The author argues that similarly, our power should attach to what Allah is powerful over without removing His power. This shows that two powers can coexist.
This refutes the objection that enabling must grant invention, because the object remains invented by God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Misconception & Correction

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
هل تشعر حقًا أن كل فعل تفعله هو في نفس الوقت فعل لله بك؟ كيف يؤثر هذا على إحساسك بالمسؤولية والتواضع في آن واحد؟
?
عندما تدرك أن قدرة الله لا تزول عن أفعالك حتى وأنت تكتسبها، هل يدفعك ذلك إلى مراقبة الله في كل حركة؟ بماذا تعد الله الآن؟
?
إن كان قياس العلم يثبت تعلق علم الله بك مع أنك تعلم بنفسك، فهل تستحي من علم الله الذي لا يزول؟ أين أنت من هذا الحياء اليوم؟

Nasafi's Analogy from Knowledge to Power in Kasb
Nasafi argues by analogy from God's knowledge to God's power, defending the Maturidi view on kasb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses an analogy between God's knowledge and power to argue that human power is not creative but acquired.

Core Idea
Just as God cannot make us know contrary to His knowledge, He cannot empower us to create contrary to His power.

Nasafi presents a sophisticated argument by analogy to defend the Maturidi position on kasb (acquisition). By comparing divine knowledge and divine power, he shows that human power cannot be creative but must be limited to actions that are 'added to' God's creation. This analogy helps clarify the relationship between divine omnipotence and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a feel for the argument's flow. Note the key terms and the structure.
Pay attention to the repeated pattern: 'just as... so too...'
2
Identify the analogy
Nasafi draws a parallel between God's knowledge (and its relation to us) and God's power (and its relation to us). Identify the two sides of the analogy.
The analogy hinges on the impossibility of God making us know something unknown to Him, and similarly empowering us to do something He cannot do.
3
Understand the key terms
Focus on 'ikhtira' (creation) and 'mudaf ilayh' (added to Him). These are crucial for the conclusion.
The argument concludes that our power is over a 'creation added to Him', not absolute creation.
4
Follow the reasoning step by step
Trace the argument: first, the servant's power cannot be creative by consensus. Then, knowledge can be shared without impossibility. The analogy from informing and empowering leads to the conclusion.
Notice the logical steps: impossibility of creative human power -> knowledge analogy -> empowering analogy -> conclusion about kasb.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand that the analogy shows human power is limited to actions that are 'added to' God's creation, not independent creation. This defends the Maturidi view of kasb.
The final sentence drives home the point: if we could have power over absolute creation, we could have knowledge of something not added to Him, which is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محال بالإجماع، فتكون قدرة العبد متعلقة لا بجهة الاختراع ضرورة، فأما كون المعلوم معلومًا بعلمين فليس بمحال فيتعلق به علمه تعالى وعلمنا، والذي يؤيد ما قلنا: أن اعتبار العلم يوجب ما ذهبنا إليه أن إعلام الغير ممن لا علم له به محال، وإنما يصح إعلام الغير ممن له العلم، فكذا إقدار الغير على شيء لا قدرة للمقدور عليه يكون محالاً، وكذا زوال العلم عما هو معلوم غيره لا يكون إلا عن جهل، فكذا زوال القدرة عما هو مقدور الغير لن يكون إلا عن عجز، فكان فيما قلتم تعجيز الله تعالى وذلك محال.

ثم نقول لهم: لما كان يستحيل أن يعلمنا الله تعالى خلاف معلومه يستحيل أن يقدرنا الله تعالى على خلاف مقدوره، ومقدوره مخترع يضاف إليه لا مطلق المخترع، فبقدرنا أيضا على مخترع مضاف إليه لا على مطلق المخترع، ولو جاز أن يقدرنا على مخترع غير مضاف إليه لجاز أن يعلمنا معلومًا غير مضاف إليه وذا باطل، فكذا هذا.
It is impossible by consensus, so the power of the servant is related not to the aspect of creation by necessity. As for something being known by two knowledges, it is not impossible, so His knowledge and our knowledge are related to it. And what supports what we said: that consideration of knowledge necessitates what we have gone to: that informing another who has no knowledge of it is impossible, and informing another is only valid from one who has knowledge. Similarly, empowering another over something for which there is no power [in the empowerer] over that which is empowered is impossible. Likewise, loss of knowledge of what is known to another does not occur except from ignorance. Similarly, loss of power over what is empowered to another would only be from incapacity. So in what you say is making God incapable, and that is impossible.

Then we say to them: Just as it is impossible for God to make us know contrary to what He knows, it is impossible for God to empower us to act contrary to what He has power over. And what He has power over is creation added to Him, not absolute creation. So we also have power over a creation added to Him, not over absolute creation. And if it were permissible for Him to empower us over a creation not added to Him, it would be permissible for Him to make us know something not added to Him, and that is false. So likewise this.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage presents an argument by analogy (qiyas) from God's knowledge to God's power. The author first states that it is impossible by consensus for the servant's power to be creative (ikhtira'). Then he argues that something can be known by two knowledges (divine and human) without impossibility, so both knowledges relate to the same object. He supports this with an analogy: informing someone who has no knowledge is impossible, but informing is valid from one who has knowledge. Similarly, empowering someone over something the empowerer cannot do is impossible. Thus, if God empowers us over something He has power over, it must be that the empowerer (God) has power over it in a special way (creation added to Him) and we have power over it in an acquired way (kasb). The conclusion is that our power is over 'a creation added to Him' (mukhtara' mudaf ilayh) not over absolute creation, because if we could have power over absolute creation, then we could have knowledge of something not added to Him, which is false. The analogy collapses if the opponent denies the analogy, but the author is asserting the parallel between knowledge and power as equally necessary.

Key Terms
قدرة
اختراع
علم
معلوم
إعلام
إقدار
مضاف إليه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That human power is creative like God's, independent of divine action.
Correction: This passage clarifies that human power is not creative; it is an acquisition over actions that are 'added to' God's creation, not absolute creation.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the analogy in this passage?
A) God's power and knowledge are identical
B) Human power cannot be creative like God's
C) Humans can create independently
D) God shares His power with humans without distinction

Key Takeaway
Human power is not creative; it is an acquisition over actions that are added to God's creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly see that sin as something you yourself created, or do you acknowledge that it is part of God's decree and that you only acquired it? How does this passage challenge your sense of personal responsibility for your sins?
?
If your power over every action is only over something 'added to God's creation,' what does that mean for your pride in your achievements? Can you really claim credit for anything you do? How should this reshape your gratitude and humility before God?
?
The analogy from knowledge to power suggests that God cannot empower you to do something He Himself has no power over. Does your daily planning assume that you can accomplish things outside God's power? How does this passage force you to realign your trust in divine omnipotence?
